#

# **Testes**

hen you want your Herói to rifle through a desk and locate a
specific document, scale a castle Parede, negotiate a treaty with a
Monarca, or undertake qualquer other activity with a chance of
Falha, you’ll need to Fazer um Teste to determine how successful you are
at the task. A Teste is qualquer Poder roll that has Falha or consequences
as an option.

When to Fazer um Teste

The Diretor should ask a jogador to Fazer um Teste only when the jogador’s
Herói attempts a task where the consequences of Falha are interesting
or dramatic, and where Falha won’t grind the story to a halt. For
example, if a Herói wants to Pulo over a waist-high Parede while casually
walking through a peaceful city neighborhood, the worst case for
Falha is probably that the Herói falls on their butt, takes no dano,
and can Levantar to either try De Novo or Andar around the Parede. As such,
no Teste is required. But if the Herói were being chased by inimigos,
failing to Pulo over the Parede means the pursuers can catch them, so the
Diretor Músculo decide to call for a Teste to determine what happens.

The advancement of a story shouldn’t be halted by failing a Teste. For
instance, the heroes Músculo need to know the color of a Anão king’s
crown to solve a puzzle, with that puzzle opening the only entrance to
a tomb they must enter to stop a world-ending ritual. It could be that a
successful Razão Teste allows the heroes to Recolher that lore, but the Teste
shouldn’t be their only option to get the information. If the Teste fails,
perhaps the heroes need to go to a flying library to do research, or they
Músculo be able to delve into a ruin to find the ancient Monarca’s portrait.
A failed Teste should always result in a story becoming more interesting,
not in the action coming to an end.

**It Just Works!**

When a Herói attempts to solve a task that typically requires a Teste with
clever, outside-the-box thinking, the Diretor can instead decide that no
Teste is required and the attempt automatically works! For example, if a
Herói who wants to Escalar a Parede first covers their hands and feet in Gigante
strands of Grudento spider webs, the Diretor Músculo decide that they can
Escalar up the Parede without needing to Fazer um Teste.

That said, such clever ideas often work for free the first time, but the
Diretor could decide they require tests if they are used De Novo.

How to Fazer um Teste

Each Teste has the following steps:

The Diretor decides that a Herói’s activities call for a Teste and asks the
Herói’s jogador to make a Poder roll using an appropriate characteristic (see
Characteristics and Tests below). The Diretor then selects a difficulty for
the Poder roll, either secretly or publicly (see Dificuldade do Teste below).

The jogador makes the Poder roll. If the personagem has a Perícia that applies
to the Teste (see Skills later in this chapter), they can ask the Diretor if
the Perícia applies and justify the use of the Perícia. If the Diretor agrees the
Perícia applies, the Herói gains a +2 Bônus to the roll.

The jogador reports the total of the roll, and the Diretor interprets its
Sucesso or Falha.

```
Characteristics and Tests
When you describe a task you want your Herói to undertake and the
Diretor determines that a Teste is necessary, they then determine
which characteristic the Teste uses based on the Natureza of the task. For
instance, if you’re scaling a Parede, the Diretor could ask for a Músculo Teste
to determine how far and how quickly you’re able to Escalar. If you’re
attempting to plead your innocence in court for a murder you didn’t
commit, the Diretor Músculo ask for a Presença Teste if you’re attempting
to win over the jury with your personality, or a Razão Teste if you’re
laying out a logical Argumento to Suporte your innocence.
Though the Diretor can decide to call for tests in qualquer circumstances,
a number of tasks that heroes routinely undertake are commonly set
up as tests.
```

```
Músculo Tests
You make a Músculo Teste whenever a risky task calls for the use of
physical strength. Músculo tests are most often used for breaking down
doors and other structures, Arremesável heavy objetos, pulling your body
up a sheer Parede, Nadador against a mighty current, and other feats of
physical Poder.
```

```
Agilidade Tests
You make an Agilidade Teste whenever a risky task calls for the use of your
physical coordination and nimbleness. Agilidade tests are most often
used for tumbling, sneaking quietly, picking locks, and engaging in
sleight of hand.
```

```
Razão Tests
You make a Razão Teste whenever you attempt a risky task that
requires the use of your mental acumen and education, formal or
otherwise. Razão tests are most often used to Recolher lore, deduce
information based on clues, complete a puzzle, forge counterfeit items
or documents, break a code, convince others of a logical Argumento, or
make an estimation.
```

```
Intuição Tests
You make an Intuição Teste whenever you attempt a risky task that
requires the use of your powers of observation and instinct. Intuição
tests are most often used to notice Escondida criaturas or details, discern
another person’s motivations or honesty, Calmaria and reassure others, and
train animals.
```

```
Presença Tests
You make a Presença Teste whenever you attempt a risky task that
requires the use of your force of personality. Presença tests are most
often used to gain trust, project confidence, and influence and Liderar
other criaturas.hough it’s easier than easy, then
```

**Dificuldade do Teste**

```
The Diretor decides how difficult a task that requires a Teste is: easy,
Médium, or hard. If a task seems as though it’s easier than easy, then
no Teste is necessary. The Herói simply accomplishes the task. If the task
seems harder than hard, then the Diretor is free to decide that it’s
impossible to complete with a Teste.
On a Teste-by-Teste basis, the Diretor can share the difficulty of a task
before the jogador makes the Teste, which makes interpreting the
outcome faster at the table. The Diretor can also keep a Teste’s difficulty
secret until after the jogador rolls the Teste, for dramatic Efeito.
```

```
The Dificuldade do Teste Outcomes table shows all the possible outcomes of
the different difficulties of tests. The Diretor will keep this information
Habilidoso so as to be able to compare the different difficulties and their
outcomes during play.
```

```
Whenever the rules talk about obtaining a Sucesso on a Teste, that
includes a straight Sucesso, a Sucesso com Consequência, or a Sucesso
with a Recompensa. Whenever the rules talk about a Falha on a Teste, that
includes a straight Falha or a Falha com Consequência.
Whenever you Fazer um Teste whose outcome you don’t like, you can
Gastar a Herói token to reroll the Teste. You must use the new roll.
```

```
Easy Tests
An Teste Fácil has some risk of consequence, but most heroes will likely
overcome it. The Poder roll you make for an Teste Fácil determines the
outcome (see Teste Outcomes below):
```

```
á You succeed on the task and incur a consequence.
é You succeed on the task.
í You succeed on the task with a Recompensa.
```

```
Médium Tests
A Médium Teste has some risk of Falha that most heroes will likely
overcome—but with a cost. The Poder roll you make for a Médium Teste
determines the outcome:
```

```
á You fail the task.
é You succeed on the task and incur a consequence.
í You succeed on the task.
```

```
Hard Tests
A Teste Difícil has a greater risk of Falha, and most heroes are likely to
suffer some hardship while trying to overcome the intended task. The
Poder roll you make for a Teste Difícil determines the outcome:
```

```
á You fail the task and incur a consequence.
é You fail the task.
í You succeed on the task.
```

```
Natural 19 or 20: Sucesso With a Recompensa
Whenever you get a natural 19 or 20 on the Poder roll for a Teste—a total
of 19 or 20 before adding your characteristic score or other modifiers—
you score a critical Sucesso. This critical Sucesso automatically lets you
succeed on the task with a Recompensa, even if the Teste has a Médium or
hard difficulty.
```

**Teste Outcomes**

```
Depending on a Teste’s difficulty and the Poder roll made to
accomplish the task represented by the Teste, you can obtain um of the
following outcomes.
```

```
Falha com Consequência
If you fail a Teste Difícil and incur a consequence, you don’t do what you
set out to do—in addition to which, you suffer an impactful setback.
The Diretor determines the exact Natureza of the consequence, which is
typically related to the specific task.
For instance, if a Herói suffers a consequence while trying to Escalar a
Parede, they Músculo make it halfway up the Parede and then fall, taking
dano and landing Derrubado. A Herói trying to Furtivo by cultists Músculo
be spotted by those foes, who immediately attack. If a consequence
strikes when a Herói attempts to bribe a prison Guarda, the Guarda Músculo
decide to Prisão the Herói or Liderar them into a Armadilha. If a Herói suffers a
consequence on a Razão Teste made to Recolher lore about the king’s
favorite meal, they Músculo confuse it for a dish to which the Monarca is
deathly allergic.
```

```
Not all consequences need to be immediate or apparent. For example,
a Herói Músculo fail with a consequence on a Teste made to cheat at a
high-stakes game of cards with a Nobre. The Falha means the cheating
is noticed, but the Diretor decides that the Nobre doesn’t say anything.
This consequence isn’t made apparent until later in the evening, when
the Nobre has guards surround the Herói, intent on taking the cheater
down to the dungeon for stacking the deck.
```

```
Influencing jogador Characters With Tests
```

```
The things jogador characters do can’t be influenced by qualquer
criatura making a Teste, whether a Monstro, an NPC, or another
jogador personagem. Many jogadores feel that their agency is taken
away if they’re compelled to Pular into a pile of gold filled
with Escondida scorpions because an NPC convinced them to do
so with a Presença Teste. For most jogadores, it’s not fun to be in
control of a Herói and lose some of that control.
```

```
Instead, Directors should do their Nível best to have an NPC
suggest that a personagem Mergulho headlong into the gold like a
billionaire duck, then let the jogador decide what their personagem
does. Similarly, a Diretor Músculo decide that um jogador
personagem can’t make an Intuição Teste to discern another PC’s
motivations or honesty.
That said, if everyone in your gaming group decides to Levantar um
or more of these restrictions after talking about it, go for it!
There’s no wrong way to play as long as everyone is having
fun. The MCDM Safety Toolkit (available for download at
https://mcdm.gg/SafetyToolkit ) discusses how to talk about
potentially problematic topics such as limiting personagem agency
at your table.
```

**Dificuldade do Teste Outcomes**

```
Poder Roll Teste Fácil Outcomes Médium Teste Outcomes Teste Difícil Outcomes
```

```
≤11 Sucesso com Consequência^ Falha Falha com Consequência^
```

```
12–16 Sucesso Sucesso com Consequência^ Falha
```

```
17+ Sucesso witha Recompensa^ Sucesso Sucesso
```

```
Natural 19 or 20 Sucesso with a Recompensa^ Sucesso with a Recompensa Sucesso with a Recompensa^
```

```
Tests
```

Common consequences for failing a Teste include the following:

¥ Making an NPC so upset that they Tempestade off, or betray, attack, or
otherwise attempt to harm you
¥ Drawing the attention of a group of foes
¥ Triggering a Armadilha or Perigo that captures or significantly harms
you or an aliado
¥ Breaking an important piece of Equipamento that is difficult to
replace or repair
¥ Thinking you know something that you don’t
¥ Getting stuck in a situation that must be resolved with a Negociação
or a Teste de Montagem you didn’t need to make before

In lieu of other consequences, the Diretor also has the option to gain 2
additional Malícia—a resource that criaturas run by the Diretor use in
Combate—no começo of the next Combate Encontro.

Falha
If you fail a Teste without incurring a consequence, you simply don’t
do what you set out to do. A Herói attempting to Escalar a Parede finds no
purchase. A Herói trying to Recolher lore can’t remember the desired facts.
If a Herói attempts to bribe a Guarda, they don’t take the bait.

On a failed Teste, the Diretor can decide that there Músculo still be a small
Penalidade for Falha, depending on the circumstances of the Teste. This
Penalidade shouldn’t be as harsh as rolling a Falha com Consequência,
though. For instance, a Herói who gets this outcome on an Agilidade Teste
made to Furtivo by a group of cultists Músculo draw the attention of um
cultist with their Falha. Now that cultist is coming to investigate, but
they haven’t raised the alarm ... yet.

When a Herói rolls a Falha without a consequence, the Diretor can
offer to let them succeed with a consequence instead. For instance,
when a Herói rolls a 10 on a Médium Músculo Teste to break down a locked
door, that’s a Falha and the door stays closed. But the Diretor could
suggest to the jogador that instead of not breaking down the door, they
can break down the door and lose 1d6 Vigor from being injured
in the effort.

Sucesso com Consequência
If you succeed on a Teste and incur a consequence, you do what you set
out to do, but with an added cost. A Herói Músculo succeed in Escalador
up a Parede, but the surface of the Parede crumbles and becomes unstable
as they do, making the Escalar more difficult for the aliado ascending after
them. When trying to Furtivo by a cultist, a Herói successfully does so,
but leaves footprints or other evidence of trespassing behind. If a Herói
bribes a Guarda to be allowed to Furtivo into a prison, the Guarda lets them
in—but then demands a gemstone the Herói needs for an important
Projeto de Criação before they let the Herói out.

Just like Falha com Consequência, the consequences accompanying
Sucesso don’t need to be immediately apparent. In lieu of other conse-
quences, the Diretor has the option to gain 2 additional Malícia at the
start of the next Combate Encontro.

When a Herói rolls a Sucesso com Consequência, the Diretor Músculo
give them a chance to fail instead. For instance, when a Herói rolls a 10
on an easy Agilidade Teste to pick the lock on a chest, that’s a Sucesso with a
consequence. The Diretor could suggest that the personagem has opened
the lock but broken their lockpicks in the process (knowing the picks
can’t be replaced until the Herói returns to town), but can also give them
the option of failing to pick the lock but keeping their lockpicks intact.

```
Sucesso
If you succeed on a Teste without consequence or Recompensa, you simply
achieve whatever you set out to do. A Herói climbs that Parede, sneaks by
those cultists, or bribes that Guarda just as they planned. Smooth.
```

```
Sucesso With a Recompensa
If you succeed on a Teste with a Recompensa, you accomplish whatever you
set out to do. But you also gain a little something extra, in the form of
momentum or luck that makes the immediate future easier for you or
your friends.
The Diretor determines the Recompensa for a Sucesso, which is most often
related to the task at hand. For instance, if a Herói succeeds with a
Recompensa while Escalador a Parede, they Músculo find a ladder at the top they
can lower so that qualquer aliados Escalador up after them can do so without
needing to Fazer um Teste. A Herói trying to Furtivo by cultists who succeeds
with a Recompensa Músculo be able to dose the cultists’ nearby Água barrel
with sleeping Veneno as they pass by unseen. Succeeding with a Recompensa
while bribing a prison Guarda could mean that the Guarda unlocks a door
for the Herói in addition to forgetting they were ever there.
```

```
As with consequences, the Recompensa that comes with a Sucesso doesn’t
need to be immediate or apparent. For example, a Herói succeeds with
a Recompensa on an Teste Fácil made to cheat at a high-stakes game of cards
with a Nobre. Not only does the Herói win the game, but the Diretor
decides that their Recompensa comes from a servant watching the game
who’s impressed with the personagem’s Atuar. After the game, the
servant approaches the Herói, offering Magia from the Nobre’s private
stash in congratulations and admiration.
Common rewards accompanying Sucesso on a Teste include
the following:
```

```
¥ Automatically accomplishing a related follow-up task that would
typically require a Teste
¥ Allowing an aliado engaged in the same task to accomplish the task
without needing to make the Teste as well
¥ Obtaining a Consumível Tesouro or useful piece of
Mundano Equipamento
¥ Learning a piece of helpful information
¥ Impressing or ingratiating yourself with someone who grants you
a small favor
¥ Noticing a Escondida danger well before it strikes, giving you time to
avoid or prepare for it
In lieu of other rewards, the Diretor can also decide that a Herói who
succeeds on a Teste with a Recompensa earns the jogadores a Herói token (see
Herói Tokens in Chapter 1: The Basics).
```

```
Regra Opcional: Pitching Consequences and Rewards
Coming up with consequences and rewards for tests can be
a big part of the fun for many Directors, but even the best
Directors occasionally run low on ideas. That’s why the
game gives the default option of consequences and rewards
in the form of Malícia and Herói tokens. However, a Diretor
who prefers narrative consequences and rewards can ask the
jogadores to pitch different consequences and rewards when
they Fazer um Teste. The Diretor can reject, add to, or modify the
jogadores’ ideas as they choose, and will remind the jogadores that
they need to pitch real consequences, and not minor rewards
disguised as consequences.
```

Draw Steel

```
How Long Does It Take?
The amount of time required for a task involving a Teste is determined
by the Diretor. A task such as recalling lore with a Razão Teste Músculo
take no time at all. Ducking behind a barrel to Esconder-se with an Agilidade
Teste Músculo require a Manobra or a Ação Principal, while tracking a
band of voiceless talkers through the World Below could take hours
or even days.
```

```
Tests During Combate
Many (but not all) tests that a Herói Músculo make during Combate are
made as maneuvers. See Maneuvers in Chapter 10: Combate for more
information.
```

**Can I Try De Novo?**

```
In many cases when you fail a Teste, you can’t attempt the Teste De Novo
unless the circumstances of the Teste change. For instance, if you attempt
an Agilidade Teste to pick a lock and fail, you can’t attempt to pick the
lock De Novo unless you get better lockpicks, oil the lock, have someone
demonstrate how to pick a similar lock, and so on.
The Diretor decides when the circumstances have changed enough to
allow a new attempt at a Teste.
```

Heroes Make Tests

```
If a Herói attempts to Furtivo by an inimigo Guarda unnoticed, should
the Herói make an Agilidade Teste to Furtivo, or should the Guarda make an
Intuição Teste to catch the Herói in the act? If a cultist lies to a Herói about
the location of a secret temple, does the cultist roll a Presença Teste to
conceal the truth, or does the Herói roll an Intuição Teste to discern the
cultist’s honesty?
```

```
Except in certain scenarios (explored at NPCs Roll for Deceptive Tasks
and Opposed Poder Rolls below), heroes make tests and NPCs do not.
Heroes are the stars of the story, and the consequences and rewards of
tests have longer-lasting implications for them. There are exceptions to
this rule, of course. If a Herói travels with an NPC Militante or companion,
that NPC will almost certainly make tests from time to time. But for the
most part, NPCs and other criaturas never need to make tests when
what they do opposes what the heroes do.
```

```
To quickly assess the difficulty of a task opposed by um or more
criaturas and the Teste made to attempt it, the Diretor can use the
following guidelines (though these are not hard and fast rules):
Teste Fácil: A Teste is easy if only um criatura opposes the Herói, and that
opposed criatura would have a lower Bônus to their Teste roll for the
task than the Herói does. If a Herói with an Agilidade score of 2 attempts
to Furtivo by a Guarda with an Intuição score of 0, the Teste is easy.
Teste Médio: A Teste is moderate if multiple criaturas oppose the Herói
and those criaturas would have lower bonuses to their Teste rolls than
the Herói, or if only um criatura opposes the Herói and has the same
Teste Bônus as the Herói.
Teste Difícil: A Teste is hard if an opposed criatura would have a higher
Bônus to their Teste roll than the Herói, or if multiple criaturas with the
same Teste Bônus as the Herói oppose the Herói.
```

```
The Falha consequences of opposed tasks are some of the easiest to
create on the Voar. Fail to Esconder-se from someone, and they notice you. Fail
to Mentir to someone, and they catch your duplicity. Fail to arm wrestle
someone for a free ale, and you’re picking up the tab. The consequence
is that the opposition bests the Herói.
```

```
Tests
```

**NPCs Roll for Deceptive Tasks**

At times, the Diretor Músculo choose for an NPC to Fazer um Teste when
engaged in a deceptive task, rather than having characters attempt
to note the deception. By having the NPC roll in these scenarios, the
Diretor doesn’t tip their hand to the jogadores that Subterfúgio is afoot.

For example, when an Assassino attempts to ambush the heroes while
they sit around a campfire, if qualquer jogador says their Herói is on the
Vigia for danger, that Herói would make an Intuição Teste to notice the
danger. But if no um is keeping watch, the Assassino makes an Agilidade
Teste to Furtivo up on the heroes unnoticed. If the Assassino fails the Teste,
the heroes notice immediately as their assailant loudly steps on a twig.
If the Assassino succeeds, the heroes don’t notice until the assailant is
right on top of them.

An NPC Músculo also make a Presença Teste if they Mentir to the heroes, as
long as the heroes have no Razão to believe the personagem would be
deceptive. The Diretor knows if the heroes are wary in that way
because the jogadores will ask if they can Fazer um Teste to discern the
NPC’s honesty.

As an Regra Opcional, the Diretor is also free to ask the heroes to make
a Teste Reativo to a deceptive NPC instead (see Reativa Tests below)
whenever they choose.

**Opposed Poder Rolls**

When dois criaturas are engaged in a particularly dramatic struggle
that requires them both to make tests, the Diretor can have all the
criaturas involved Fazer um Teste. The criatura with the highest Poder roll
wins. You can’t earn a Recompensa as part of these opposed Poder rolls, and
they don’t follow the typical difficulty structure or have três different
tiers of possible outcomes.

For example, if your Herói attempts to Furtivo by a Demônio lord, you make
an Agilidade Teste to Mover stealthily while the Demônio makes an Intuição
Teste to notice you. If your Herói gets the higher Poder roll, you Furtivo
by without the Demônio noticing. If the Demônio gets the higher roll, they
catch you in the act of sneaking. If multiple sneaking heroes attempt
to get by multiple demons, then each criatura makes a Teste and all the
totals are compared to determine which demons notice which heroes.

In the event of a tie in an opposed Teste, the state of the scene doesn’t
change. In the previous example, a tie means that if a Demônio on Guarda
duty didn’t know a sneaking Herói was there, the Demônio remains
oblivious. If the Demônio did know the Herói was out there somewhere
while trying to avoid being noticed, a tie means the Demônio still knows
the Herói is there but hasn’t determined their location.

Since opposed Poder rolls don’t use tiers, when you make an opposed
Poder roll, a double Vantagem provides a +4 Bônus to the roll, a double Desvantagem
provides a -4 Penalidade to the roll, an automatic Grau increase counts as
a +4 Bônus to the roll, and an automatic Grau decrease counts as a -4
Penalidade to the roll.

Reativa Tests

At certain times when a Herói isn’t engaged in overcoming a task,
the Diretor Músculo ask the jogador of the Herói to Fazer um Teste without
context, explaining the Teste only after the Poder roll is made. This often
happens when a Herói has a chance of knowing or noticing something
of significance that the jogador doesn’t know to look for or ask about.

Reativa tests are typically made in the following circumstances,
though the Diretor can call for them in qualquer appropriate scenario:

```
Escondida Environmental Features: The Diretor asks for an Intuição
Teste to notice a secret door, a Escondida Armadilha, or some other disguised
environmental Recurso.
Escondida Foes: The Diretor calls for an Intuição Teste to
notice a Escondida foe (or they could use the rules in
NPCs Roll for Deceptive Tasks above).
Escondida Motives: The Diretor can ask for an Intuição Teste during a
conversation to gauge how well a Herói can read an NPC, judging
whether they’re lying, withholding information, or concealing
an emotional response. (The Diretor could also use the rules in
NPCs Roll for Deceptive Tasks.)
Recolher Lore: The Diretor Músculo ask a Herói to make a Razão Teste
when dealing with a new objeto, a piece of information, or an
event to determine what História or details the Herói Músculo already
know about it.
criatura and DTO Tests: Some criaturas and dynamic terrain objetos in
Draw Steel: Monstros have features and abilities that require heroes
to make Reativa tests. These tests can’t be modified by skills.
```

```
Regra Opcional: Secret Reativa Tests
Some Directors prefer to make the Poder rolls for Reativa
tests for the heroes rather than asking the jogadores to do so.
This allows the Diretor to make the rolls when appropriate
for Escondida objetos, criaturas, motivations, and information
without tipping off the jogadores that there is information to
be gained. Having the Diretor roll requires the Diretor to
have everyone’s characteristics and skills recorded (whether
physically or digitally) for easy reference.
```

Draw Steel

```
Skills
Skills represent the different specializations a Herói has outside of
attacking, defending, and using their Linhagem features, Classe features,
and Equipamento. Whenever you Fazer um Teste, having a particular Perícia
associated with the Teste increases your chance of Sucesso.
```

**Applying Skills**

```
If you have a Perícia that applies to a Teste you make, you gain a +2 Bônus
to the Teste. For instance, if your Herói has the Esconder-se Perícia, you have a +2
Bônus to qualquer Teste you make that involves hiding yourself. This Músculo
include an Agilidade Teste to Esconder-se behind a barrel, or a Presença Teste to
disappear into a crowd.
The +2 Bônus gained for a Perícia isn’t an Vantagem. A jogador can Fazer um Teste
that has both the +2 Bônus for a Perícia and the +2 Bônus for an Vantagem.
```

```
You can’t apply more than um Perícia to a Teste.
```

```
Justify the Perícia
It’s not the Diretor’s job to know every task potentially covered by the
skills in the game, or to know the specific skills your Herói has. Instead,
the Diretor asks you to Fazer um Teste using a characteristic and you tell
the Diretor if you think you have a Perícia that applies. If it’s not obvious
why the Perícia applies, tell the Diretor how your Herói is approaching
the task and justify why that approach uses the Perícia. The Diretor
then decides if you get the +2 Bônus the Perícia represents. If the Diretor
disagrees with you, that’s the final word.
Approaching problems creatively while remaining reasonable can
help you get the most out of your skills. For example, if you’re making
a Presença Teste to impress a Nobre at a party, using the Gabar-se Perícia is an
obvious choice. But what if you don’t have that Perícia? Maybe you could
instead try to impress the Nobre with a brief but exciting lecture about
the Natureza of the elements, making a Presença Teste using the Magia Perícia
that you do have!
```

```
Sometimes you won’t have a Perícia that applies to a Teste. That’s okay!
If your characteristic score is decent, you likely have a good chance of
Sucesso without a Perícia.
```

```
Mixing Characteristics and Skills
Although certain skills are often paired with um characteristic more
than others, a Perícia can apply to a Teste made using qualquer characteristic that
makes sense. The Diretor has the final say on which characteristic is
used to complete a task, and can call for a different characteristic based
on the circumstances.
For example, intimidating someone with a purely verbal threat is a
Presença Teste. But if a jogador describes their personagem tearing a log in
half with their bare hands to Intimidar a foe, the Diretor is likely to
call for a Músculo Teste instead. The Intimidar Perícia can apply to both tests.
In the same way, scaling the side of a building is covered by a Músculo
Teste, but if a Herói does a series of leaps from um balcony to another to
Alcance a roof, the Diretor could call for an Agilidade Teste instead. The Escalar
Perícia applies to both of these tests.
```

**Many Specific Skills**

```
Draw Steel includes a big list of skills, and each is fairly specific. For
example, instead of um Athletics Perícia that covers Escalador, jumping,
Nadador, and lifting heavy objetos, your personagem Músculo use separate
Escalar, Pular, Levantar, and Nadar skills. Instead of a Thievery Perícia that covers
picking locks, picking pockets, and disabling traps, the game has três
skills: Arrombar Fechadura, Furtar, and Sabotar.
```

```
Having a wide Alcance of specific skills means you’ll frequently make
tests that don’t use um of your personagem’s skills, simply applying a
characteristic. By not having a few broader skills, it means that having
a personagem who covers the spread of every Perícia is actually impossible.
Luckily, the math of the game doesn’t require you to have a Perícia to have
a decent chance of Sucesso on a Teste. That means heroes can attempt
tasks without the help of a Perícia just because someone needs to do it,
and that’s pretty darn heroic!
```

```
Since you don’t need to worry about your personagem covering a wide
spread of skills, you’re free to choose the skills you think fit your Herói
best and are the most fun to work with. Maybe you’re thinking about
an Elementalista who has a gymnastic Antecedentes in jumping and
tumbling, and who also studied Religião and Forja. Having
that kind of specific backstory is a big part of cinematic storytelling.
The rules for skills allow for them to be flexibly applied to qualquer Teste that
is appropriate for the Perícia. This encourages clever thinking. A jogador can
ask the Diretor, “I want to impress the duke with a story about how
I ascended the sheer Cliffs of Azgahnan. Can I use my Escalar Perícia for a
+2 Bônus to my Presença Teste?” Getting Criativa like that is a lot of fun.
It paints a visual picture, and it’s good tactical thinking! However, if the
skills in a game are too broad in the kinds of activities they represent,
jogadores inevitably end up applying the same Perícia over and over De Novo to
as many tests as possible. This isn’t fun for anyone, and doesn’t make a
very compelling story.
```

```
Edges on Tests With Specific Skills
```

```
Certain features and abilities grant a criatura an Vantagem on tests
made with a specific Perícia. A criatura making a Teste where the
specific Perícia would apply gains an Vantagem on the Teste even if
they don’t have the Perícia. For example, the Conduíta’s Blessing
of Fortunate Weather can create Tempo Enevoado weather that grants
criaturas who make tests using the Esconder-se Perícia an Vantagem on those
tests. qualquer criatura who attempts to Esconder-se in the Névoa gains an
Vantagem on the Teste as long as the Esconder-se Perícia would apply to that
Teste, regardless of whether they have that Perícia or not.
```

```
Are All Skills Equal?
When choosing skills for your personagem, deciding which
skills will be most useful depends a lot on the campaign. For
instance, the Nadar Perícia Músculo be used constantly during
a campaign that takes place on the ocean and has heroes
exploring underwater ruins, but it won’t come up as much in a
campaign that takes place entirely in a vast desert. The Psiônica
Perícia Músculo come up a lot in a campaign where voiceless talkers
are the main foes, and Magia Músculo be more useful in a game
where the heroes take on a circle of evil wizards. If you’re
worried about whether a Perícia you’d like to take will be useful,
discuss your Perícia list with the Diretor after you create a Herói.
And if a Perícia doesn’t work out, you can always Comércio de Almas it for
another Perícia as you wish (see Changing personagem Options in
Chapter 2: Making a Herói).
```

```
Tests
```

**Perícia Groups**

Skills are broken down into five Perícia groups: crafting, exploration, inter-
personal, intrigue, and lore.

Perícias de Criação
Skills from the crafting Perícia group are used in the Criação and appraisal
of goods and for jury-rigging contraptions. They are especially useful
during rests and downtime.

Rewards for tests made with Perícias de Criação typically include having
leftover rare material used in the Criação process, knowing a buyer
willing to pay extra for goods or items you’re appraising, or making a
jury-rigged device so amazing that it lasts for more uses than it should.

Consequences for tests made with Perícias de Criação typically include
wasting rare materials used in the Criação process, greatly overesti-
mating or underestimating an item’s value, and poorly jury-rigging a
contraption so that it harms people (or at least the wrong people).

```
Perícias de Criação
Perícia Use
Alquimia Make bombs and potions
Arquitetura Create buildings and vehicles
Forja Forge metal armor and weapons
Carpintaria Create items out of wood
Culinária Create delicious dishes
Flecharia Make À Distância weapons and ammunition
Falsificação Create false badges, documents, and other items
Joalheiria Create bracelets, crowns, rings, and other Joalheiria
Mecânica Build machines and clockwork items
Alfaiataria Craft clothing of cloth or leather
```

```
Perícias de Exploração
Perícia Use
Escalar Mover up Vertical surfaces
Conduzir Control vehicles
Resiliência Remain engaged in strenuous activity over a long period of time
```

```
Ginástica Mover across unsteady or narrow surfaces; tumble
Curar Use Mundano first aid
Pular Pulo Vertical and horizontal distances
Levantar Pick up, carry, and Jogar heavy objetos
Navegação Read a map and travel without becoming lost
Montar Montar and control a nonsapient Montaria, such as a cavalo
Nadar Mover through deep liquid
```

Perícias de Exploração
Skills from the exploration Perícia group are used to physically explore the
Ambiente around the characters, and to overcome physical obstacles.

Rewards for tests made with Perícias de Exploração typically include helping
another criatura engaging in the same task succeed without needing
to also Fazer um Teste, automatically succeeding on a follow-up Teste while
engaged in the same task, reaching a destination faster than anticipated,
and learning about or avoiding an upcoming Perigo.

Consequences for tests made with Perícias de Exploração include harming
yourself, your Equipamento, or your aliados; becoming lost; or stumbling headlong
into a Perigo or a place you were trying to avoid.

Perícias Interpessoais
Skills from the interpersonal Perícia group are used to socially interact
with other criaturas, and are particularly useful during negotiations
(see Chapter 11). Aside from the Trato Animal Perícia, you can
generally only use Perícias Interpessoais when you attempt to influence
criaturas who have emotions and who can understand you.

Rewards for tests made with Perícias Interpessoais typically include
gaining an extra favor, item, or piece of information from the people or
criaturas you interact with.

Consequences for tests made with Perícias Interpessoais include making
the criatura you’re interacting with angry, sad, embarrassed, offended,
or otherwise upset or uncomfortable. This Músculo cause them to ignore
you, Tempestade off, spread Boatos about you, attack you, betray you,
blackmail you, or otherwise attempt to harm you.

```
Perícias Interpessoais
Perícia Use
Gabar-se Impress others with stories of your deeds
Empatizar Relate to someone on a personal Nível
Flertar Attract romantic attention from someone
Apostar Make bets with others
Trato Animal Interact with nonsapient animal wildlife
Interrogar Obtain information from a criatura withholding it
Intimidar Espantar or scare a criatura
Liderar Inspire people to action
Mentir Convince someone that a falsehood is true
Música Perform Música vocally or with an instrument
```

```
Perform Engage in dance, oratory, acting, or some other physical Atuar
```

```
Persuadir Convince someone to agree with you through use of your charms and grace
```

```
Ler Pessoas Read the emotions and body idioma of other criaturas
```

Draw Steel

```
Perícias de Conhecimento
Skills from the lore Perícia group are used to research and Recolher specific
information. They are especially useful during rests and downtime.
```

```
Rewards for tests made with Perícias de Conhecimento typically include learning an
extra piece of useful information.
Consequences for tests made with Perícias de Conhecimento typically include learning
an incorrect piece of information that seems useful, but which actually
works against your interests or wastes time. (It’s fun to roleplay these
kinds of moments, so lean in!) Alternatively, the Diretor can make
Médium and hard tests with lore group skills for each Herói in secret,
then let the jogadores know the narrative outcome without revealing the
outcome of the Poder roll (see the Regra Opcional: Secret Reativa Tests
sidebar earlier in this chapter).
```

```
Perícias de Intriga
Perícia Use
Atenção Intuitively sense the details of your surroundings
Conceal objeto Esconder-se an objeto on your person or in your Ambiente
Disfarce Change your appearance to look like a different person
Bisbilhotar Actively listen to something that is hard to hear, such as a whispered conversation through a door
```

```
Escapar Escape from bonds such as rope or manacles
Esconder-se Conceal yourself from others’ observation
Arrombar Fechadura Receptivo a lock without using the key
Furtar Steal an item that another person wears or carries without them noticing
```

```
Sabotar Desativar a mechanical device such as a Armadilha
Procurar Actively Procurar an Ambiente for important details and items
```

```
Furtivo Mover silently
Rastrear Follow a trail that another criatura has left behind
```

```
Perícias de Conhecimento
Perícia Use
```

```
Criminoso Underworld Knowing about Criminoso organizations, their crimes, their relationships, and their leaders
Cultura Knowing about a Cultura’s customs, folktales, and taboos
História Knowing about significant past events
Magia Knowing about magical places, spells, rituals, items, and phenomena
```

```
Monstros Knowing Monstro ecology, strengths, and weaknesses
Natureza Knowing about natural flora, fauna, and weather
```

```
Psiônica Knowing about Psiônica places, spells, rituals, items, and phenomena
Religião Knowing about religious mythology, practices, and rituals
Boatos Knowing gossip, legends, and uncertain truths
Sociedade Knowing Nobre etiquette and the leadership and Poder dynamics of Nobre families
```

```
Estratégia Knowing about battle tactics and logistics
Timescape Knowing about the many worlds of the timescape
```

```
Perícias de Intriga
Skills from the intrigue Perícia group are used in tasks centered around
investigation, thievery, and spycraft.
Rewards for tests made with skills from this group typically include
helping another criatura engaging in the same task succeed without
needing to also Fazer um Teste, automatically succeeding on a follow-up
Teste while engaged in the same task, discovering helpful information
in addition to what you set out to learn, and performing an extra bit of
clandestine activity in addition to what you set out to do.
```

```
Consequences for tests made with Perícias de Intriga include getting caught
in the act or failing to notice a detail that places you in danger, such as
triggering a Armadilha or walking into an ambush.
```

```
For the Diretor: Make Your Own Skills
Directors should feel free to make their own skills that they
feel are relevant and useful to their campaigns and adventures.
For instance, the game doesn’t have a Brewing Perícia for brewing
ale or a Painting Perícia for making art because those aren’t tasks
that typically come up in a game about fighting Monstros and
saving the world. However, a Diretor could decide that their
campaign involves poisoned barrels of ale and large amounts
of counterfeit art, and that adding these dois new skills to the
game would make it more fun for the jogadores. The Diretor
simply needs to pick a group for these new skills—in this case,
crafting makes sense. They then let the jogadores know that they
can swap out qualquer crafting Perícia they have for these new skills.
```

```
Tests
```

Example Tests

In this scenario, a trio of adventurers want to scale the 40-foot-high
walls surrounding a castle known as the Star Chamber, hoping to
covertly obtain information about their inimigo, Lady Morgant.

**Diretor (Matt):** _The towering walls that surround the Star Chamber
stand before you, the single Ferro gate closed and locked, with a Pelotão of
armed guards outside._

**James (playing Korvo, a Sombra):** _Let’s Mover to the side of the Parede
opposite the gate and make our ascent there._

**Grace (playing Val, a Conduíta):** _Agreed._

**Diretor:** _Okay. It’ll be a Músculo Teste to get up to the top of the Parede._

The Diretor knows that the walls around the Star Chamber, the head-
quarters of the evil knights Lady Morgant leads, are smooth and hard
to Escalar, designed to Repelir invaders. The Teste’s difficulty is hard, but the
Diretor keeps that information a secret for now.

**Alyssa (playing Jorn, a Tático):** _Let me go first. I’ve got good Músculo and can
Jogar the others down a rope once I’m up there. And I’ve got the Escalar Perícia._

**Diretor:** _For sure. Okay, roll it up._

Alyssa rolls 2d10 and gets a 13. She then adds her Músculo score of 2 and
her +2 Bônus for having an applicable Perícia to the roll, for a total of 17.

**Alyssa:** _A 17! That’s Grau 3, baby!_

The Diretor checks the Dificuldade do Teste Outcomes table to confirm that
a Grau 3 outcome is a Sucesso on a Teste Difícil.

**Diretor:** _Okay, you’re on top of the Parede. You notice a few guards
patrolling atop the opposite side of the Parede in the Distância, but they’re
looking out at the city right now._

**Alyssa:** _Great! I Lançamento down a rope. Val, you’re next._

**Grace:** _So it’s a Músculo Teste. Would you let me use Resiliência? It’s a lot of
physical exertion to Escalar._

**Diretor:** _It’s not a Escalar that would take you hours, so I don’t think
Resiliência applies here. But hey, the rope does make this an easier Teste._

**Grace:** _Fair. Okay, dice. Let’s do this._

Given the rope, the Diretor decides that this second Escalar attempt is
an Teste Fácil. Grace rolls 2d10 and gets an 11. With her Músculo score of 2,
that’s a 13.

**Grace:** _13! That’s a Grau 2 outcome for Val._

The Diretor checks the Dificuldade do Teste Outcomes table once more,
confirming that a Grau 2 outcome is a Sucesso on an Teste Fácil.

**Diretor:** _Good news! You make it to the top of the Parede alongside Jorn._

**James:** _Ah, crap. I have a Músculo of −1 and no skills to use. Unless I can
Intimidar the rope into lifting me up?_

**Diretor:** _Wishful thinking._

**Alyssa:** _What if Korvo grabs onto the rope and I Levantar him up while he just
hangs on for the Montar?_

**Diretor:** _Sure. That’ll be a Músculo Teste if Korvo’s down for it._

**James:** _Nothing risked, nothing saved. Let’s do it. Just be careful. qualquer loud
noises could attract those guards._

```
Alyssa: Please. I’m a pro. Since I’m lifting this polder off the Chão, does
the Levantar Perícia apply?
```

```
Diretor: Yes, it does. Roll it up. That’s a Médium difficulty Teste.
Lifting the diminutive polder, Alyssa rolls 2d10—but gets a 2! With her
Músculo score and Levantar Perícia Bônus of +2, the total is 6.
```

```
Alyssa: A 6! Oof. That’s Grau 1.
Diretor: Which is a Falha, but with no consequence. You realize you
just can’t Levantar Korvo off the Chão without making a lot of noise.
```

```
The Diretor then decides to make the Falha potentially more
interesting, by allowing the jogadores to decide if they want a Falha
without consequence or a Sucesso com Consequência.
Diretor: I’ll give you a choice, though. You can leave Korvo on the
Chão, or Puxar him up and suffer the consequence of making some noise
while doing so.
```

```
Grace: Ah, Puxar the polder up.
Alyssa: Yeah. We have to face these guards sometime.
```

```
James: Thanks for not leaving me behind!
Diretor: As Jorn yanks Korvo off the Chão and pulls him up to the top
of the Parede, a Guarda turns a bullseye lantern your way, calling out, “Who
goes there?”
```

Draw Steel

```
Auxiliar um Teste
You can attempt to assist another criatura with a Teste they make,
provided you have a Perícia that applies to the Teste, the other criatura
isn’t using that same Perícia on the Teste, and you can describe how your
personagem helps to the Diretor’s satisfaction. In other words, your
attempt to help has to make sense, and you have to bring some useful
expertise to the table. Helping another criatura Furtivo by shouting
encouragement at them isn’t going to make them stealthier.
```

```
When you attempt to assist another criatura, Fazer um Teste using the Perícia
you choose, and using a characteristic chosen by the Diretor based on
the activity you use to help. The outcome of that Teste determines the
Bônus applied to the Teste you’re assisting:
```

```
á You get in the way or make things worse. The criatura takes a
Desvantagem on their Teste.
é Your help grants the other criatura an Vantagem on their Teste.
í Your help gives the other criatura a double Vantagem on their Teste.
For example, when an aliado tries to pick a jailer’s pocket, you Músculo
attempt to assist by using the Flertar Perícia to distract the jailer. The
Diretor accepts this, and asks you to make a Presença Teste using Flertar.
The outcome of that Teste determines the Bônus you provide to the
other Herói’s Agilidade Teste to pick the jailer’s pocket—or whether you
fumble the distraction and potentially draw attention to the attempt.
```

Esconder-se and Furtivo

```
Hiding and sneaking are important tools for heroes and their foes. You
Músculo want to avoid another criatura’s notice to Bisbilhotar on conver-
sations, steal items, set up an ambush, or avoid a Combate Encontro.
```

```
Hiding
To Esconder-se from a criatura, you must have Cobertura or Encobrimento from that
criatura (see Chapter 10: Combate), who can’t observe you attempting
to Esconder-se. A criatura is observing you if they’re aware of your specific
location before you attempt to Esconder-se. This means they can pinpoint you
with their senses and point a finger (or paw or Tentáculo) at you as if to
shout, “There they are!” If you duck behind a barrel to Esconder-se from a foe,
your attempt to Esconder-se has a chance of succeeding only if your foe doesn’t
notice you doing so. If you’re being chased by a hungry Dragão, you can
Esconder-se only if you first Mover to a location where the Dragão can’t observe
you—for instance, by turning a sharp corner into a tunnel full of Gigante
stalagmites before the Dragão does. You then make your Esconder-se attempt.
```

```
When you use the Esconder-se Manobra to Esconder-se during Combate while you
have Cobertura or Encobrimento from a criatura who isn’t observing you,
you are automatically Escondida from them unless the Diretor deems
otherwise. If you Esconder-se fora de Combate, the Diretor Músculo ask you to
Fazer um Teste using the Esconder-se Perícia to determine how well Escondida you are.
While you are Escondida from another criatura, the criatura can’t alvo
you with abilities that don’t have the Área Palavra-Chave. This Benefício ends
as soon as you are no longer Escondida from that criatura.
```

```
Additionally, while you are Escondida from another criatura, you gain an
Vantagem on Habilidade rolls made against that criatura. This Benefício lasts until
the end of the Turno in which you are no longer Escondida. This means you
can be Escondida from another criatura no começo of your Turno, Mover out
of Cobertura or Encobrimento toward them and use an Habilidade against them,
and still gain an Vantagem on Habilidade rolls made against the criatura as long
as you use the Habilidade before the end of that Turno.
```

```
Tests
```

You are no longer Escondida from a criatura if you don’t have Cobertura or
Encobrimento from them. If you use an Habilidade, interact with an inimigo,
Mover without sneaking, or otherwise make noise or reveal yourself
while Escondida, you are no longer Escondida once the activity that reveals
you resolves. For instance, if you are Escondida and then make a Golpe, you
resolve the Golpe first, then are no longer Escondida.

Searching for Escondida criaturas
You can Procurar for criaturas who are Escondida from you as long as those
criaturas are within 10 squares and you have Linha of Efeito to them. To
do so, you use a Manobra to make an Intuição Teste using the Procurar
Perícia, and qualquer Escondida criaturas within 10 squares of you each make
an opposed Agilidade Teste using the Esconder-se Perícia (see Opposed Poder Rolls
earlier in this chapter). At the Diretor’s discretion, different charac-
teristics and skills can be used in this opposed Teste. For example, your
foe Músculo make a Presença Teste using the Trato Animal Perícia to Esconder-se
among a flock of sheep without disturbing them, or you could make
a Razão Teste using the Bisbilhotar Perícia to pick out the breathing of a
criatura Escondida in the dark.

If the total of your Teste is higher than that of a Escondida criatura, they are
no longer Escondida from you. Otherwise, they remain Escondida from you.
As part of the Manobra used to Procurar Criaturas Escondidas, you can
point out qualquer criaturas you notice to aliados within 10 squares of you,
making those criaturas no longer Escondida from those aliados.

If a criatura is Escondida from your aliados but not from you, you can
use a Manobra without making a Teste to point that criatura out to
your aliados.

```
Sneaking
While you are Escondida from another criatura and not durante o Combate, you
can attempt to Furtivo—avoiding the senses of other criaturas as you
Mover around them in the Receptivo—to remain Escondida. While sneaking,
your Velocidade is halved. To Furtivo, you make an Agilidade Teste using the Furtivo
Perícia with a difficulty set by the Diretor. If you succeed, you remain
Escondida during your Movimento. This Teste can use another characteristic
at the Diretor’s discretion, such as using Presença to blend in with a
crowd on a packed city street.
```

```
What Does It Mean to Be Observed?
Most of the time, if a criatura has Linha of Efeito to you, they’re
able to observe you—especially if you’re an active threat to
them, such as in a Combate Encontro. However, the game leaves
what it means to be observed Receptivo to interpretation, because
there are circumstances where a criatura Músculo have Linha of
Efeito to you but isn’t observing you, giving you a chance to
Esconder-se. For example, a Guarda in a crowded marketplace likely
isn’t able to observe every criatura within their Linha of Efeito, so
slipping away to Esconder-se in that situation is probably easier than
hiding from them in an otherwise empty street. The Diretor
has the final say on who is observing you, and who you are
able to observe.
```

Draw Steel

```
Group Tests
Whenever dois or more heroes attempt to overcome a single, simple
task together that calls for them to make the same Teste, the Diretor
can call for a Teste de Grupo. For example, if several heroes are all attempting
to Escalar the outside of a tower at the same time, giving each other
assistance and advice, they could be asked to make a Músculo Teste de Grupo.
If a group of heroes attempt to Furtivo by a sleeping Ogro, they Músculo
make an Agilidade Teste de Grupo.
```

**Teste de Grupo Difficulty**

```
The Diretor determines the difficulty of a Teste de Grupo the same way
they do for individual tests. Group tests can be easy, Médium, or hard.
```

```
Making a Teste de Grupo
Each Herói participating in the Teste de Grupo makes the Teste individually
as usual, but the Diretor waits until all the tests have been made to
interpret the outcome. A Herói who is participating in the Teste de Grupo
can’t assist another Herói participating in the Teste.
```

```
Teste de Grupo Outcome
When interpreting the outcome of a Teste de Grupo, the Diretor first
determines if the task succeeded or not before figuring out rewards
and consequences. If half or more of the heroes making the Teste de Grupo
succeed, then the Teste de Grupo succeeds. Otherwise, the Teste de Grupo fails.
```

```
If the heroes succeeded and half or more of them obtained a Recompensa
from the Teste, the Diretor gives the group a collective Recompensa and
ignores qualquer consequences incurred in the Teste. This collective Recompensa
should be equivalent to earning dois individual rewards. In fact, it could
be dois Consumível items, juicy pieces of information, or Herói tokens.
However, it could also be something more tailored to the task. For
instance, if the heroes earn a collective Recompensa while sneaking through
the camp of an inimigo army, the Diretor Músculo allow them to Sabotar
a bunch of Guerra engines or steal a few horses on their way out.
If the heroes failed the Teste de Grupo and more than half of them incurred
a consequence as a result, the Diretor gives the group a collective
consequence and ignores qualquer earned rewards. This collective
consequence should affect everyone. An easy option is for the stress of
failing the Teste to cause each Herói to take a Desvantagem on their next Poder
roll, or for the Diretor to gain 2 Malícia per Herói no começo of the
next Combate Encontro. But the consequence could also be tailored
to the task. For instance, if the heroes fail in their attempt to Furtivo
through the camp of an inimigo army, they’re spotted and the camp
immediately goes on alert as waves of inimigos attack them.
```

```
If fewer than half the heroes incur a consequence or earn a Recompensa on
their individual tests, then the Teste de Grupo simply succeeds or fails.
```

```
Tests
```

Montage Tests

When a group of heroes works together over time to accomplish
a common goal that requires more than a single characteristic, the
Diretor can call for a Teste de Montagem. Such tests typically take place
over a prolonged period and Foco on collective or shared activities.
Navigating a vast desert, convincing farmers to rise up against a
tyrannical Líder, and performing a ritual to Receptivo a magically sealed
gate can all be accomplished with montage tests.

In a Teste de Montagem, the jogadores take turns making tests as their
characters Ombrada a task together in a Teste de Montagem Ronda. Each Herói has
a chance to Fazer um Teste (or to assist another Herói’s Teste; see Auxiliar um Teste
above) intended to influence the outcome of the task.

A Herói can also Gastar their Turno using an item, Habilidade, or other
option they have available that they believe can help in the montage
Teste. For example, if a group of heroes want to cross an ocean on a
sailing ship before a Tempestade begins, um Herói Músculo make use of a
Magia fan that creates wind to keep the sails full day and night. The
Diretor decides that this clever action gives the heroes 2 automatic
successes in the Teste de Montagem, with no individual tests necessary (see
Total Successes and Failures below).

Once a Herói makes a Teste, assists with a Teste, or uses an Habilidade or
other option, they can’t do anything else as part of the Teste de Montagem
until each other Herói involved in the Teste de Montagem does so as well. A
Herói can also choose to do nothing, most often if they have no um to
assist and fear that their actions Músculo make the situation worse (see
Teste de Montagem Outcomes below). Once every Herói has had a chance to
act, the Teste de Montagem Ronda ends and a new um begins.

**Time and Stakes**

As the name suggests, montage tests create a kind of cinematic
montage in the action of the game. A Teste de Montagem can take place over
the course of several hours or days, with each individual Teste or other
activity set up as a brief vignette within the montage that stars um of
the heroes. Combate encounters, negotiations, and other challenges and
scenes can break up a Teste de Montagem (see Sample Teste de Montagem below).

The Diretor should deploy montage tests only when the jogadores are
engaged in overcoming a goal that has stakes for the story and some
sort of pressure, such as a looming deadline or impending harm. A
Teste de Montagem is great for a race to get to another location before an
inimigo army does, a chase to escape or catch up to a foe, weathering
a Perigo, preparing a village for Guerra, or similar activities. Low- or
no-stakes activities such as travel through a forest with no time
pressure, or training during a Descanso to use a new kit, can be narrated in
montage style, but they don’t require a Teste de Montagem.

**Diretor Sets the Scene**

no começo of a Teste de Montagem, the Diretor should describe the scenario
underlying the task at hand, and the various challenges the heroes
Músculo face as they attempt to collectively accomplish it. For example, if
the heroes are chasing down a pickpocket through a crowded market,
the Diretor Músculo talk about the throngs of innocent people Posicionamento de Palco
the way forward, obscuring the characters’ Visão, and making noise
that complicates attempts to hear the thief ’s Ligeiro footsteps. There
are also traveling carts to dodge, the Velocidade and dexterity of the pursued
personagem to contend with, and a Bando of stray dogs who chase after
anyone who sprints through the market. Describing these obstacles
gives the heroes ideas about what they’re trying to overcome as they
attempt to achieve their goals.

```
Individual Tests in Montage Tests
The difficulty of each individual Teste in a Teste de Montagem is set by the
Diretor and can vary from Teste to Teste. For instance, if the heroes are
preparing the defenses of a village threatened by a band of approaching
raiders, the Diretor Músculo decide that a personagem who wants to Cavar a
trench around the village needs to make an easy Músculo Teste. Another
Herói wants to train the untested farmers of the village in the ways of
Guerra, and the Diretor decides this is a hard Razão Teste.
```

```
The same rules and guidelines that apply to all individual tests apply
in montage tests. If a Herói has a clever, out-of-the-box idea that the
Diretor thinks should automatically succeed without rolling dice, it
does. If the circumstances of the Teste should grant an Vantagem or a Desvantagem,
they do. Individual Teste outcomes shouldn’t halt the story.
The Diretor should couch each Sucesso or Falha as it relates to the
overall goal of the Teste de Montagem. If the heroes are trying to Alcance an
ancient temple, failing a Músculo Teste to ford a river in their path doesn’t
mean they don’t cross the river and are stuck on the other side. But it
could mean that failing to cross the river in a timely manner gives a
Rival group of villains the chance to beat the party to the temple.
```

```
The rewards and consequences of individual tests made during a
Teste de Montagem are handled on an individual basis. The Diretor can use
the default of gaining additional Malícia in the next Combate Encontro
for consequences and having the party gain Herói tokens for rewards to
keep the montage moving.
```

```
Can’t Use the Same Perícia Twice
An individual personagem can’t use the same Perícia more than once in a
Teste de Montagem. Though multiple heroes can use the same Perícia, a Teste or
an assist with a specific Perícia represents each characters’ entire contri-
bution to the Teste de Montagem with that Perícia. At the Diretor’s discretion,
this restriction can be lifted for prolonged montage tests, or for montage
tests that are limited in scope and have only a small number of skills
that apply to them.
```

**New Challenges for Each Teste**

```
In general, when a Herói makes a Teste as part of a Teste de Montagem, they
should choose new obstacles to overcome that haven’t already been
overcome as part of the Teste. If the heroes are chasing a thief through
the marketplace and um of them has already Distraído the Bando of
stray dogs with a deft hand and a piece of meat, additional tests made to
distract the animals don’t count toward the outcome of the Teste de Montagem.
When it fits the scenario, the Diretor can adjust this restriction. If part
of a Teste de Montagem involves searching for people trapped in a Queimando
building, the Diretor is likely to allow multiple tests to fight or avoid the
Fogo, since this will happen throughout the Teste de Montagem, not just once.
```

```
Introducing More Challenges
During a Teste de Montagem, a Diretor can introduce new challenges for
the heroes to face. While attempting to run out of a Queimando building
from the top floor, the characters Músculo discover that by the time they
Alcance the second floor, beams are starting to fall and glass windows are
exploding as the structure starts to collapse. These new challenges can
be incorporated into the tests the heroes subsequently make.
```

Draw Steel

```
Sucesso Total
If the heroes earn a Sucesso Total, they achieve what they set out to do
without Complicação. For instance, if the heroes engaged in a montage
Teste to cross a desert and Alcance a city before a tyrant’s army arrives there
and levels the place, a Sucesso Total sees them arrive at the city gates
with plenty of time to warn people of the impending assault.
The heroes earn 1 Vitória when they achieve Sucesso Total on an easy
or moderate Teste de Montagem, and 2 Victories on a hard Teste de Montagem.
```

```
Sucesso Parcial
If the heroes earn a Sucesso Parcial, they succeed at what they set out
to do, but there is a Complicação or a cost involved. For instance, when
crossing the desert to Alcance and warn the city of the tyrant’s army,
a mixed Sucesso sees the characters arrive at the city gates with the
inimigo forces just behind them. Alternatively, the Diretor Músculo allow
the heroes to arrive well before the army, but they don’t Cobertura their
movements well enough. The tyrant realizes the city has been warned
and decides to call in a favor to have a powerful Dragão join the siege.
```

```
The heroes earn 1 Vitória when they achieve Sucesso Parcial on a hard
or moderate Teste de Montagem.
```

```
Falha Total
If the heroes suffer Falha Total, they don’t achieve what they set out
to do. Just as with standard tests, Falha on a Teste de Grupo shouldn’t bring
a story to a halt. Falha Total should make things more interesting and
challenging! With a Falha Total in a Teste de Montagem to cross the desert
and warn the city, the characters arrive at the city to find it already
under siege by the tyrant.
```

```
Sample Teste de Montagem
Four heroes must cross the vast and inhospitable Deserto Infinito
to warn the city of Ahset that the tyrannical Empress Vardo is
coming to conquer them. If the characters arrive in time, they can
organize the defenses of the city, giving its people a greater chance of
defeating the tyrant.
```

```
The Diretor determines that crossing the desert is a Teste de Montagem of
hard difficulty. With four heroes involved, the Limite de Sucesso is 6 and the
Limite de Falha is 2 as the Teste de Montagem begins.
```

```
Teste de Montagem Ronda 1
When the Teste begins, the Diretor sets the scene. They tell the jogadores
that the desert has extreme temperatures, sudden sandstorms, high
dunes to cross, deep sand, chasms, and Areia Movediça lakes. The Diretor
decides that the challenges of dunes, deep sand, and Areia Movediça can be
tackled multiple times in the Teste, since the Deserto Infinito is filled with
these hazards.
Urdoncara, a Fúria, starts things off by asking to make an Intuição Teste
using the Natureza Perícia to predict the best times of day to travel and
rest. She wants the party to avoid the worst of the desert’s extreme
temperatures and qualquer sandstorms or other weather phenomena, so
that the journey is quickened. The Diretor decides this is an Teste Fácil.
Urdoncara makes the Teste and gets a total of 12, earning 1 Sucesso for
the Teste de Montagem.
```

```
Jorn, a Tático, wants to make a Razão Teste using the Escalar Perícia to
Liderar the party over dunes and other hazards with minimal effort. The
Diretor allows the attempt, but says that knowing what makes um
dune easier to Escalar than another is tricky, setting the difficulty at
hard. Jorn gets a 9 on the Teste and fails with a consequence, which the
Diretor decides will cause him to take a Desvantagem on his next Poder roll
due to the exertion. The Teste de Montagem has 1 Sucesso and 1 Falha.
```

```
Total Successes and Failures
The Diretor or another jogador will Rastrear the total number of successes
and failures the heroes earn during a Teste de Montagem. Every Teste de Montagem
has a Limite de Sucesso and a Limite de Falha. When the number of successful
tests equals the Limite de Sucesso, the Teste de Montagem ends and the heroes
achieve Sucesso Total (seeMontage Teste Outcomes below). The montage
Teste can also end when the number of failed tests equals the Falha
limit, and the heroes suffer Falha Total.
```

**Limited Rounds**

```
A Teste de Montagem should last only 2 Teste de Montagem rounds. If the heroes
don’t end the Teste de Montagem by achieving the Limite de Sucesso or Falha
limit, the Teste de Montagem ends when the second Teste de Montagem Ronda is
over. This time limit helps to keep a Teste de Montagem from becoming a
slog, and prevents heroes from simply using their turns to assist the
um Herói with the best chance of Sucesso. This can inspire each Herói to
be a more active participant in the Teste de Montagem. That said, the Diretor
can increase the number of rounds a Teste de Montagem lasts if they wish to
create a particularly grueling Desafio.
```

```
Teste de Montagem Difficulty
The Diretor determines the Limite de Sucesso and Limite de Falha of a montage
Teste. They can share this information or keep it secret, depending on
what feels the most fun and dramatic for the situation and the jogadores.
```

```
In general, the higher the Limite de Sucesso, the harder and more
complicated it is for the heroes to overcome the Teste de Montagem, since a
Herói can’t make the same Teste twice. The Teste de Montagem Difficulty table
gives a recommended Limite de Sucesso and Limite de Falha for easy, moderate,
and hard montage tests for groups with five heroes.
```

```
Teste de Montagem Difficulty
Difficulty Limite de Sucesso Limite de Falha
Easy 5 5
Moderate 6 4
Hard 7 3
```

```
For larger or smaller groups, the Diretor can make the following
adjustments to keep montage tests achievable but challenging:
```

```
¥ For four or fewer heroes, decrease the Limite de Sucesso and Falha limits
by 1 (to a minimum of 2) for every Herói fewer than five. For example,
if a group has only três heroes, an easy Teste de Montagem has a Sucesso
limit and Limite de Falha of 3.
¥ For six or more heroes, increase the Sucesso and Falha limits by 1 for
every Herói more than five.
```

```
Teste de Montagem Outcomes
A Teste de Montagem can have três different outcomes:
```

```
¥ If the heroes hit the Limite de Sucesso before hitting the Limite de Falha or
before the time runs out for the Teste, they achieve Sucesso Total.
¥ If the heroes hit the Limite de Falha or time runs out, and if they’ve
achieved at least dois more successes than failures, they achieve a
Sucesso Parcial.
¥ If the heroes hit the Limite de Falha or time runs out, and if they
don’t have at least dois more successes than failures, they suffer
Falha Total.
```

```
Tests
```

Karrel, an Elementalista, thinks the group Músculo cross the desert faster
if they have specially modified sandshoes that distribute their weight
and prevent their feet from sinking into the sand. The Diretor loves the
idea, and decides that making four pairs of the shoes while traveling the
desert is a Médium Razão Teste. Karrel gets to use their Alfaiataria Perícia
and winds up with a total of 13—a Sucesso com Consequência. The
Diretor decides to gain an additional 2 Malícia no começo of the next
Combate Encontro as a consequence, but the group now has 2 successes
and 1 Falha on the Teste de Montagem.

Val, a Conduíta, offers to Batedor ahead for the group with an Intuição
Teste, using the Navegação Perícia to find the best path forward and avoid
hazards such as chasms and Areia Movediça. The Diretor thinks that acting
as Vigia in a vast desert is an easy task. Val smashes it with a 21—a
Sucesso with a Recompensa—and the Diretor decides to get Criativa. Val’s
Vigia skills grant the next Herói to act in the Teste de Montagem an Vantagem on
their Teste. At the end of the first Teste de Montagem Ronda, the heroes have 3
successes and 1 Falha.

Interlude
Before the next Teste de Montagem Ronda, the Diretor pauses the montage
Teste to run a battle with a Minhoca das Fendas Real, who attacks the heroes as
they cross over an ancient ruin partially buried in the sand. After the
heroes defeat the Minhoca das Fendas Real, the Teste continues.

Teste de Montagem Ronda 2
Urdoncara wants to make a Músculo Teste using the Levantar Perícia to carry most
of the group’s Equipamento as they cross the desert, allowing her aliados
to Mover more quickly while she keeps up with her superior fortitude.
The Diretor thinks this arduous task has a hard difficulty. Urdoncara
gets a 17 on the Teste thanks to the Vantagem from Val’s earlier Sucesso. The
Teste de Montagem has 4 successes and 1 Falha.

Jorn, eager to prove himself after his last Falha, asks to make a Músculo
Teste using the Liderar Perícia, representing tying a rope around his waist to
drag his weaker friends over the tallest dunes. The Diretor likes the
idea but doesn’t think the Liderar Perícia applies to the task. They tell Jorn
that Levantar is more appropriate, since the Tático is using his physical
Perícia to aid his friends and not really doing anything interpersonal. Jorn
agrees, and the Diretor sets the Teste at Médium difficulty. Making
the Teste with a Desvantagem because of his previous Falha, the Tático rolls
a 15, which is a Sucesso com Consequência. The Teste de Montagem has 5
successes and 1 Falha, but the consequence gives the Diretor another
2 Malícia no começo of the next Combate Encontro.

Since the group needs only um more Sucesso to achieve Sucesso Total,
Karrel says she’d like to assist Val in whatever task she decides to take
on. Val wants to Recolher lore about the Khem-hor—the inhabitants of
the Deserto Infinito—to remember their time-honored travel techniques
using the História Perícia. Karrel has the Cultura Perícia, which she can use
to assist by providing information about the lives and Sociedade of the
Khem-hor. She makes a Razão Teste to assist and gets a 16, granting Val
an Vantagem on her upcoming Teste.

Val attempts to Recolher lore about the Khem-hor, wanting to know if she
can remember qualquer of their travel from her studies of the História of the
region. The Diretor has her make a hard Razão Teste with an Vantagem,
thanks to Karrel’s input on the current state of Khem-hor Cultura. Val
gets a 17, and the Diretor decides that the Conduíta recalls a shortcut
through a canyon tunnel that leads directly to Ahset, avoiding a vast
lake of Areia Movediça. The heroes get their sixth Sucesso in the montage
Teste, achieving Sucesso Total, and earn 2 Victories.

```
Other Options
The heroes could have attempted other tests during their travels,
such as an Agilidade Teste using the Furtivo Perícia to Liderar the group through
dangerous shortcuts in the desert without being seen or waylaid by
predators, a Razão Teste using the Natureza Perícia to find enough food and
Água to keep the group hydrated and fed, or a Presença Teste using the
Música Perícia to inspire aliados to travel faster with song.
```

```
Combate
```

```
Chapter 10
```

```
Sides
Every Combate Encontro is a conflict between dois sides. The heroes
and qualquer of their aliados are um side, controlled by the jogadores. qualquer
criaturas who oppose the heroes are the other side, controlled by
the Diretor. All criaturas who oppose the heroes are on the same
side, even if those criaturas also oppose each other. For example, if
the heroes are battling a group of bandits when a Minhoca das Fendas Real
suddenly bursts into the fray to devour jogador characters and brigands
alike, the Minhoca is still on the side of the bandits for the purpose of the
game’s Combate rules.
```

```
Combate Ronda
Combate takes place over a series of Combate rounds. During a Combate
Ronda, each criatura in the battle takes a Turno. Once every criatura has
taken a Turno, a new Ronda begins.
```

**When Does Combate Start?**

```
Combate starts as soon as um criatura intends to harm another, or
when some environmental Efeito is in a position to deal dano to or
impose other negative effects on um or more criaturas. This means
that even before the action happens, a Herói can’t use a heroic Habilidade
without spending their Recurso Heróico on it, because Combate has
already begun!
```

# **Combate**

```
hen the heroes face a problem that can be solved only with
action, or when they come up against criaturas who want to
harm them, it’s time to Jogar down!
```

Set the Map

When Combate begins, the Diretor should position miniatures or
tokens on a gridded map to represent the Ambiente, the heroes,
their foes, and qualquer other criaturas in the battle.

**Tamanho and Space**

A criatura’s Tamanho indicates how many squares they occupy during
Combate, which defines the criatura’s space. If a criatura’s Tamanho is 1, they
occupy a space of 1 Quadrado. If a criatura is larger than 1 Quadrado, their
Tamanho equals the number of squares they take up in length, width, and
height. For example, a cavalo has a Tamanho of 2, which means that during
Combate, they occupy a space that is 2 squares long, 2 squares wide, and
2 squares high. You could also think of that space as a Cubo that is 2
squares on all sides.

The minimum amount of space a criatura can take up during Combate is
1 Quadrado, but Tamanho 1 criaturas can run the Alcance from tiny pixies to small
polders, Médium humans, and large Hakaan. As such, for criaturas of
Tamanho 1, that Tamanho is further broken down as 1PP, 1P, 1M, or 1G—abbrevia-
tions for tiny, small, Médium, and large. Tamanho 1PP is um Tamanho smaller than
Tamanho 1P, dois sizes smaller than 1M, três sizes smaller than 1G, and four
sizes smaller than Tamanho 2. If a mechanic mentions Tamanho 1 criaturas, that
mechanic applies to all criaturas of Tamanho 1.

objetos also have a Tamanho rating, which usually indicates how many
squares they occupy. Some objetos are identified as having an irregular
Tamanho, with that Tamanho instead representing the objeto’s mass and weight
relative to a criatura of the same Tamanho. If a mechanic mentions objetos of
a certain Tamanho, that mechanic includes all objetos of that Tamanho, including
irregular objetos.

The criatura Sizes table shows example sizes for criaturas up to Tamanho
5, but larger sizes are possible. There is no limit to what a criatura’s
Tamanho Músculo be.

```
NPC aliados
If an NPC aliado fights alongside the heroes, the Diretor should
give the jogadores the aliado’s Ficha de Criatura and let them control
the NPC during Combate. The Diretor has enough to worry
about. As well, qualquer missteps, mistakes, or triumphs the aliado
makes will be thanks to the decisions of the jogadores and not
the Diretor, which can make the outcome of the battle more
satisfying for the jogadores.
```

```
criatura Sizes
Tamanho Example criatura
1PP Pixie
1P Polder
1M Humano
1G Hakaan
2 Ogro
3 Arbusto Cambaleante
4 Gigante da Colina
5 Dragão de Agouro
How Big is a Quadrado?
It’s helpful to know how big a Quadrado is for abilities and features
that heroes and NPCs can use fora de Combate. By default,
a Quadrado is 5 feet on all sides. But the Diretor can change
this measurement to 2 yards, 2 meters, 1 meter, or qualquer other
measurement you prefer, as long as that scale stays consistent
throughout your game.
```

Draw Steel

```
Determine Surprise
When battle starts, the Diretor determines which criaturas, if qualquer, are
caught off Guarda. qualquer criatura who isn’t ready for Combate no começo
of an Encontro is Surpreso until the end of the first Combate Ronda. A
Surpreso criatura can’t take triggered actions or free triggered actions,
and Habilidade rolls made against them gain an Vantagem.
```

```
For example, if the heroes Furtivo up unnoticed on a camp of marauders
and attack, each Saqueador is Surpreso. Likewise, if the heroes fail to
notice that all the cloaked figures in a tavern are actually brain-de-
vouring zombies, then the heroes are Surpreso. If um of the heroes
notices the disguised Morto-Vivo before the zombies attack but has no
opportunity to warn their aliados, that Herói isn’t Surpreso but the rest of
the characters are.
```

```
Determine Who Goes First
Sometimes figuring out who gets to take the first Turno durante o Combate is
automatic. If all the criaturas on um side are Surpreso, then a criatura
on the other side gets to act first. But if both sides have criaturas who
aren’t Surpreso, the Diretor or a jogador they choose rolls a d10. On a 6
or higher, the jogadores determine who goes first—the heroes’ side or the
other side. Otherwise, the Diretor decides which side goes first.
```

```
criaturas Take Turns
Whichever side goes first chooses a criatura (or sometimes a group of
criaturas on the Diretor’s side) to act no começo of Combate. Whenever
the rules talk about a criatura acting durante o Combate, that criatura gets
to take their Turno. When that Turno is over, the other side chooses a
criatura to act. Play continues back and forth this way as each criatura
takes their Turno.
```

```
Unless an Habilidade or Especial rule allows them to do so, qualquer criatura who
has taken a Turno during a Combate Ronda can’t act De Novo until a new
Ronda begins. To help Rastrear which criaturas have already acted in the
current Ronda, each criatura can have a coin, token, or card they flip
over on the table, or some kind of flag they set on their virtual tabletop
token, once they’ve taken a Turno. That way, all the jogadores know who
has already acted and who hasn’t.
In many encounters, a point comes when um side has criaturas who
haven’t acted yet but all the criaturas on the other side have. The
criaturas who have yet to act get to take their turns in qualquer Ordem they
choose, without turns in between from the other side. For example,
consider four heroes taking on six inimigos. When all four heroes
```
