```
have taken their turns and four of the inimigos have taken theirs,
the dois inimigos who are left take their turns um after the other to
end the Ronda.
```

```
Determining Who Acts Next
When it comes to the heroes’ side, the choice of who should act next is
intended to give jogadores the opportunity to comment, strategize, and
plan. Some tables, in some encounters, Músculo find that the choice of
who should act next isn’t obvious, Conduzindo to debate. That’s fine. Delib-
erating about what the group should do next is classic roleplaying.
```

```
In general, though, most groups find that it’s usually only um or dois
jogadores in a given Ronda who think it best if they act next. And as soon
as those jogadores explain why they want to act next and what they plan
on doing, the issue is quickly resolved.
```

```
Argumento Timer
If the jogadores do end up arguing in circles about what to do next, the
Diretor can place a timer on the discussion. Usually, giving the jogadores
a warning and 30 seconds to decide who goes next does the trick.
If they can’t choose by the end of that time, the Diretor chooses a
Herói to act.
```

```
Alternative Turno Ordem
If planning everyone’s Turno Ordem isn’t fun for your group, you
can leave it to the dice instead. no começo of Combate, have
each Herói, inimigo, and group of inimigos make an Agilidade Teste,
then record the totals. When it’s time for someone on the
heroes’ side to act, the Herói with the highest total goes first.
On the next Herói Turno, the Herói with the second-highest total
takes their Turno, and so on. The Diretor-controlled criaturas
act the same way. criaturas on the same side should reroll tied
Agilidade tests to determine who among the tied criaturas acts
before the others.
At the Diretor’s discretion, a Herói can swap their Turno in the
Ordem with another willing Herói no começo of a new Combate
Ronda. This allows certain abilities that interact with the
core Turno Ordem system, such as the Sombra’s Hesitation Is
Weakness Habilidade, to better work with this alternative system.
```

```
Combate
```

inimigos Act In Groups
Diretor-controlled criaturas act in groups, with information for
building groups found in _Draw Steel: Monsters_. When a group of
inimigos acts, the Diretor chooses a single criatura or Lacaio Esquadrão
to take a Turno. Once that Turno is over, the Diretor chooses another
criatura in that group to take a Turno, continuing until all members of
the group have taken their Turno.

**End of Ronda**

Once all criaturas on both sides of a battle have acted, the Combate
Ronda ends and a new Combate Ronda begins. The side whose
members acted first during the initial Combate Ronda goes first in all
subsequent rounds.

Agindo em seu Turno

Each criatura durante o Combate—whether Herói, adversary, or something in
between—gets to take a **Ação Principal** , a **Manobra** , and a **Ação de Movimento**
on their Turno (explained later in this chapter). Each combatant can
perform their Manobra and Ação Principal in qualquer Ordem, and can break up
the Movimento granted by their Ação de Movimento before, after, or between
their Manobra and Ação Principal however they like. You can also Turno
your Ação Principal into a Ação de Movimento or a Manobra, so that your Turno
can alternatively consist of dois Mover actions and a Manobra, or dois
maneuvers and a Ação de Movimento.

The Movimento section below breaks down how your Ação de Movimento
works, while the Maneuvers and Main Actions sections break
down the baseline maneuvers and main actions your personagem can
undertake. For qualquer activities not specifically covered in those rules,
such as cutting down a chandelier to drop on inimigos, the Diretor
decides whether such an activity is a Manobra or a Ação Principal.

**Triggered Actions and Free Triggered**

**Actions**

Your Herói Músculo have um or more unique triggered actions, each of
which has a specified Gatilho that allows the action to be used. You
can use um Reação per Ronda, either on your Turno or another
criatura’s Turno, but only when the action’s Gatilho occurs. For instance,
a Fúria Herói can use the Linhas de Força Reação to force Mover a
alvo, but only after an inimigo has first tried to force Mover the Fúria or
another nearby criatura.

A Reação Livre follows the same rules as a Reação, but
it doesn’t count against your limit of um Reação per Ronda. For
instance, a Sombra Herói can use their Hesitar é Fraqueza Habilidade to
take their Turno in response to the Gatilho of another Herói ending their
Turno. But because that Habilidade is a Reação Livre, the Sombra can
still use their No Meio da Confusão Reação later in the Ronda.

If multiple triggered actions occur in response to the same Gatilho, qualquer
heroes and other jogador-controlled criaturas taking a Reação
or a Reação Livre decide among themselves which of those
triggered actions are resolved first. Then the Diretor decides the same
for criaturas they control.

qualquer Efeito that prevents you from using triggered actions also prevents
you from using free triggered actions.

```
Free Maneuvers
Boring stuff like opening an unlocked door, picking up an arrow from the
Chão, giving an objeto to an Adjacente aliado, or drawing a Arma doesn’t
require a Manobra or a Ação Principal. Rather, you can undertake such
straightforward activities as free maneuvers on your Turno. A Manobra Livre
follows the same rules as a regular Manobra, but you can typically take as
many free maneuvers as you like.
```

```
At the Diretor’s discretion, circumstances could make something that is
typically boring more impactful and exciting. For instance, if you need to
pick a Magia arrow up off the Chão during a violent earthquake, what
would otherwise be a Manobra Livre could require a Manobra or a main
action to accomplish.
Likewise, the Natureza of an activity Músculo make it too complicated for a free
Manobra. For example, picking up the body of an Inconsciente Talento aliado
to carry them to safety can probably be done as a Manobra Livre. But if
your Músculo is lacking and you need to pick up a Tático aliado decked out
in the Armadura Brilhante kit, the Diretor Músculo determine that you need to
use a regular Manobra to hoist their armored form over your shoulders.
```

```
qualquer Efeito that prevents you from using maneuvers also prevents you
from using free maneuvers.
```

```
No-Action Activities
Free maneuvers Cobertura most of the simple activities you Músculo want
to undertake on your Turno. When it isn’t your Turno, you can typically
undertake even simpler activities requiring no action with the Diretor’s
approval. For instance, shouting out a warning to an aliado or dropping an
item so another criatura can pick it up require no action.
```

```
The Diretor can limit what kinds of no-action activities you can attempt
when it isn’t your Turno. For instance, shouting out a warning about an
unseen foe to an aliado on the aliado’s or the foe’s Turno requires no action.
But the Diretor Músculo stop you from giving that aliado complex tactical
advice when it isn’t your Turno, saying that doing so instead requires a free
Manobra on your Turno.
```

```
Movimento
During Combate, criaturas can employ multiple Mecânica that allow
them to Mover around the battlefield. The most common of those
Mecânica is the Avançar or Retirar-se Ação de Movimento (detailed under
Mover Actions below), but abilities granted by your Classe, Equipamento,
Linhagem, Título, or other options Músculo allow you other ways to Mover.
```

```
Your Herói starts with a Velocidade granted by their Linhagem—usually 5. This
represents the maximum number of squares you can Mover when you
take the Ação de Movimento or when another Efeito allows you to Mover. Your
Velocidade can be increased by your kit and other game options.
All squares Adjacente to your personagem cost 1 Movimento to Mover into. No,
there’s no Pythagorean theorem on the grid. It’s a game, don’t overthink it.
```

```
Your Herói can Mover freely through an aliado’s space. You can Mover through
an inimigo’s space, but that space is Terreno Difícil (see below). You can’t
stop moving in qualquer other criatura’s space, including to make a Golpe or use
a Ação Principal or Manobra while in that space and then continuing your
Mover, unless that criatura’s Tamanho is dois or more sizes greater or smaller
than your own.
At the Diretor’s discretion, you can be forced into the same space as
another criatura whose Tamanho is within 1 of yours, such as by Caindo down
a narrow shaft with such a criatura already at the bottom. When you are
squeezed into the same space as another criatura whose Tamanho is within 1 of
yours, your Habilidade rolls and tests take a Desvantagem.
```

Draw Steel

```
Can’t Exceed Velocidade
A single Mover or other Efeito can never allow a criatura to Mover
more squares than their Velocidade, unless the Efeito states otherwise. For
example, a criatura with Velocidade 5 Músculo have that Velocidade reduced to 2
by the Lento Condição (see Conditions in Chapter 5: Classes). If an
aliado then alvos them with an Efeito that allows them to Mover up to
3 squares, the criatura can Mover only 2 squares because that’s their
current Velocidade.
```

**Can’t Cut Corners**

```
A criatura can’t Mover diagonally when doing so would involve passing
through the corner of a Parede or some other objeto that completely fills
the corner between the criatura’s space and the space they are moving
to. This rule applies only to moving past objetos, not moving past
other criaturas.
```

```
Cut Corners
The Tático moves 3 squares to exit the building without
cutting corners. The Cão de Guerra Eviscerita can’t Mover around the
side of the building in just 2 squares of Movimento, since they’d
have to cut a corner to do so.
```

**Shifting**

```
Shifting is a careful form of Movimento that allows a criatura to Mover
safely past dangerous foes. Certain abilities, features, and other rules
allow you to Ajustar-se a specific number of squares, sometimes up to your
Velocidade. Whenever you Ajustar-se, criaturas can’t make opportunity attacks
against you triggered by that Movimento (see Opportunity Attacks later
in this chapter).
You can’t Ajustar-se into or while within Terreno Difícil or Terreno Danoso
(see below). If a rule allows you to Ajustar-se, you can choose to instead Mover
up to the number of squares you would have shifted (for example, to
get out of Terreno Difícil). However, you can’t combine moving and
shifting within that Movimento.
```

**Movimento Types**

```
criaturas in the game can use eight types of Movimento: Andar, Escavar,
Escalar, Nadar, Pular, Rastejar, Voar, and Teleportar-se.
```

```
Andar
Walking is the most common Movimento Tipo, whether it refers to
ambulating on legs, rolling, slithering, or some other default method
of Movimento. Unless specified otherwise, all criaturas can Mover over
solid horizontal Chão without qualquer problem.
```

```
Escavar
A criatura who has “Escavar” in their Velocidade entry, or who gains the
temporary Habilidade to Escavar, can Mover through dirt horizontally, and
either has the means to breathe while doing so or doesn’t require Ar
to live. Such criaturas can’t Mover through more solid Chão, such as
Pedra, unless their Ficha de Criatura or the Efeito that lets them Escavar says
otherwise. Similarly, a Escavador criatura doesn’t leave a tunnel unless
the rules say so.
Cavar Manobra
It takes extra effort to Cavar vertically through the Chão as opposed to
tunneling horizontally, requiring a criatura to use a Especial Manobra. To
use the Cavar Manobra, a criatura must have “Escavar” in their Velocidade entry,
they must have a Velocidade that is equal to or greater than their Tamanho, and they
must be touching terrain that can be burrowed through.
```

```
When a criatura uses the Cavar Manobra, they can Mover vertically up to a
number of squares equal to their Tamanho. If a Escavador criatura has a criatura
who is not Inconsciente Agarrado, they can’t willingly Mover deeper into the
Chão. It’s too difficult to Cavar with a flailing inimigo in your Garras.
Targeting Escavador criaturas
If you are on the Chão, you have Linha of Efeito to a Escavador criatura if
that criatura occupies 1 or more squares of terrain that can be burrowed
through and that touch the Chão, and if you have Linha of Efeito to qualquer of
those squares. The Escavador criatura gains the Benefício of Cobertura from you.
```

```
If you are completely beneath the Chão while Escavador, you don’t have
Linha of Efeito to qualquer criatura on the surface unless a rule states otherwise.
If you are completely beneath the Chão while Escavador and are
Adjacente to another criatura who is Escavador, you have Linha of Efeito to
that criatura, though you both have Cobertura from each other.
```

```
You can’t gain the Benefício of high Chão (see below) against criaturas who
are completely beneath the Chão while Escavador.
Non-Escavador criaturas
If you are on the Chão and Adjacente to a criatura who is beneath the
Chão while Escavador, you can use a Manobra to Puxar that criatura
up 1 Quadrado out of the Chão, provided the criatura is willing.
```

```
If a criatura who can’t Escavar wants to Cavar into the Chão, they can
use the following Habilidade provided their Velocidade is 2 or more.
```

```
Cavoucar
— Manobra
e Personagem x Personagem
```

```
Poder Roll + Músculo :
á You can Mover 1 Quadrado into, out of, or through Chão you are
touching that can be burrowed through, and you are Lento
and Enfraquecido (FdT).
é You can use your Ação Principal this Turno to Mover 1 Quadrado
into, out of, or through Chão you are touching that can be
burrowed through, and you are Lento (FdT).
í You can Mover 1 Quadrado into, out of, or through Chão you are
touching that can be burrowed through.
```

```
Escavador Movimento Forçado
While a criatura who is completely beneath the Chão while
Escavador is force moved by Movimento that isn’t Vertical, they aren’t
moved, and they take 1 dano for each Quadrado they would have been
force moved. If the Movimento Forçado is Vertical, the criatura is moved
through the dirt as is if were Ar.
```

```
Combate
```

Escalar or Nadar
A criatura who has “Escalar” in their Velocidade entry, or who gains the
temporary Habilidade to automatically Escalar, can Escalar across Vertical and
horizontal surfaces at full Velocidade. Likewise, a criatura who has “Nadar” in
their Velocidade entry, or who gains the temporary Habilidade to automatically
Nadar, can Nadar in liquid at full Velocidade.

criaturas without those types of Movimento can still Escalar or Nadar
when a rule allows them to Mover, but each Quadrado of Escalador or
Nadador costs 2 squares of Movimento. If a surface is difficult to Escalar
(for instance, a sheer cliff or ice-covered Parede) or a liquid is hard to Nadar
through (a raging river or whirlpool), the Diretor can call for a Músculo Teste.
On a Falha, a criatura can’t Escalar or Nadar but wastes no Movimento in
the attempt. The Diretor can also impose other consequences to Falha,
such as being caught in the spinning current of a whirlpool.

**Escalador Other criaturas**
You can attempt to Escalar a criatura whose Tamanho is greater than yours. If
the criatura is willing, you can Escalar them without qualquer trouble. If the
criatura is unwilling, you make the following Teste:

```
Poder Roll + Músculo or Agilidade :
á You fail to Escalar the criatura, and they can make a Golpe Simples
against you.
é You fail to Escalar the criatura.
í You Escalar the criatura.
```

While you Escalar or Montar a criatura, you gain an Vantagem on Corpo-a-corpo abilities
used against them. The criatura can use a Manobra to attempt to
knock you off, forcing you to make the following Teste:

```
Poder Roll + Músculo or Agilidade :
á You fall off the criatura into an unoccupied Adjacente space of
your choice, taking Caindo dano and landing Derrubado as usual
(see Caindo below).
é You Deslizar down the criatura into an unoccupied Adjacente
space of your choice and don’t land Derrubado.
í You continue to hold on to the criatura.
```

If you are knocked Derrubado while Escalador or riding a criatura, you fall
and land Derrubado in an Adjacente space of your choice, taking dano as
usual from the fall.

Pular
Whenever an Efeito allows you to Mover (including using the Avançar
Ação de Movimento), you can automatically long Pular a number of squares up
to your Músculo or Agilidade score (your choice; minimum 1 Quadrado) as part
of that Movimento. The height of your Pular is automatically 1 Quadrado as
part of that Movimento.

If you want to Pular even longer or higher than your baseline Pular
allows, make a Músculo or Agilidade Teste:

```
Poder Roll + Músculo or Agilidade :
á You don’t Pular qualquer farther than your baseline Pular allows.
é You Pular 1 Quadrado longer and higher than your baseline Pular
allows.
í You Pular 2 squares longer and higher than your baseline
Pular allows.
```

You can’t Pular farther or higher than the Distância of the Efeito that
allows you to Mover. You can’t Pular out of Terreno Difícil or damaging
terrain (see below).

```
Rastejar
If you are Derrubado (see Conditions in Chapter 5: Classes), you can remain
Derrubado and Rastejar on the Chão. Doing so costs you 1 additional Quadrado
of Movimento for every Quadrado you Rastejar. If you intentionally want to
Rastejar, you can fall Derrubado as a Manobra Livre. While voluntarily Derrubado,
you can choose to stand as a Manobra Livre.
```

```
F ly
A criatura who has “Voar” in their Velocidade entry, or who gains the
temporary Habilidade to Voar, can Mover through the Ar vertically or horizon-
tally at full Velocidade and remain in midair. If a flying criatura is knocked
Derrubado or has their Velocidade reduced to 0, they fall (see Caindo below).
```

```
Pairar
A criatura who has “Pairar” in their Velocidade entry (most commonly
alongside “Voar” or “Teleportar-se”), or who gains the temporary Habilidade to
Pairar, can remain motionless in midair. They don’t fall even if they are
knocked Derrubado or their Velocidade is reduced to 0.
```

```
Teleportar-se
When a criatura teleports, they Mover from um space to another space
instantaneously. The following rules apply to teleporting:
¥ Teleporting doesn’t provoke opportunity attacks or other effects that
are triggered by a criatura moving.
¥ When a criatura teleports, they bypass qualquer obstacles between the
space they leave and their destination space.
¥ A criatura teleporting themself must have Linha of Efeito to their
destination space. A criatura teleporting another criatura must have
Linha of Efeito from the space the teleported criatura leaves and to
their destination space.
¥ A teleporting criatura’s destination space can’t be occupied by
another criatura or objeto.
¥ The Efeito that lets a criatura Teleportar-se indicates how far they can
Teleportar-se. That Distância can be greater than the criatura’s Velocidade.
¥ If a criatura can Teleportar-se as part of their usual Movimento, they can
use the Avançar Ação de Movimento to Teleportar-se a number of squares up to
their usual Velocidade, unmodified by conditions or effects.
¥ If a criatura teleports while Derrubado, they can be standing when they
Alcance their destination space provided they are able to stand. If a
Derrubado criatura is teleported by another criatura, it is up to that
criatura whether the teleported criatura remains Derrubado or stands if
they are able.
¥ If you Teleportar-se while affected by the Agarrado or Imobilizado conditions,
those conditions end for you.
¥ When a criatura teleports, they must leave the space where they
start and enter a new space. A criatura can’t Teleportar-se to and from
the same space.
```

**Caindo**

```
When a criatura falls 2 or more squares and lands on the Chão, they
take 2 dano for each Quadrado they fall (to a maximum of 50 dano)
and land Derrubado. A criatura who falls can reduce the effective height
of the fall by a number of squares equal to their Agilidade score (to a
minimum of 0). Caindo into liquid that is 1 Quadrado or more deep reduces
the effective height of a fall by 4 squares (to a minimum of 0).
Caindo is not Movimento Forçado, but being force moved downward is
considered Caindo (see Caindo below). Movimento from Caindo doesn’t
provoke opportunity attacks (see Opportunity Attacks below).
```

Draw Steel

```
Caindo Onto Another criatura
A criatura who falls and lands on another criatura causes that criatura
to take the same dano from the fall. The Caindo criatura then lands
Derrubado in the nearest quadrado desocupado of their choice. If the Caindo
criatura’s Tamanho is greater than the Músculo score of the criatura they land
on, that criatura is knocked Derrubado.
```

```
Caindo Far
When a criatura first falls from a great height, they fall 100 squares in
the first Ronda. At the end of each subsequent Ronda that they remain
Caindo, they fall another 100 squares.
```

```
Terreno Difícil
Areas of thick underbrush, rubble, spiderwebs, or other obstacles
to Movimento create Terreno Difícil. It costs 1 additional Quadrado of
Movimento to enter a Quadrado of Terreno Difícil.
```

**Terreno Danoso**

```
Areas of Ácido, Fogo, sharp rocks, lava, or qualquer other terrain that causes
dano to criaturas within it is Terreno Danoso. The dano dealt
by Terreno Danoso is noted in the terrain’s description or in the
description of the Efeito that creates the terrain.
High Chão
Whenever a criatura uses an Habilidade to alvo a criatura or objeto while
standing on the Chão and occupying a space that is fully above the
alvo’s space, they gain an Vantagem on the Poder roll against that alvo. To
be fully above a alvo, the bottom of a criatura’s space must be higher
than or bordering on the top of the alvo’s space.
```

```
A criatura can gain this Benefício while Escalador only if they have
“Escalar” in their Velocidade entry or can automatically Escalar at full Velocidade
while moving.
```

```
Movimento Forçado
Some actions and maneuvers allow a criatura to Empurrar, Puxar, or Deslizar a
alvo criatura or objeto a specific Distância across the battlefield. Collec-
tively, these types of Movimento are called Movimento Forçado.
```

```
Empurrar X: The criatura moves the alvo up to X squares away from
them in a straight Linha, without moving them vertically. Each
Quadrado the criatura moves the alvo must put the alvo farther
away from them.
Puxar X: The criatura moves the alvo up to X squares toward them
in a straight Linha, without moving them vertically. Each Quadrado the
criatura moves the alvo must bring the alvo closer to them.
Deslizar X: The criatura moves the alvo up to X squares in qualquer Direção,
except for vertically. Unlike a Empurrar or a Puxar, a Deslizar doesn’t need to
be a straight Linha.
When you force Mover a alvo, you can always Mover that alvo fewer
squares than the number indicated. For example, when the Conduíta
obtains a Grau 3 “Empurrar 3” outcome with their Invocar o Trovão
Habilidade, they can Empurrar alvos qualquer Distância up to 3 squares, including
choosing to not Mover certain alvos at all.
```

```
Movimento Forçado ignores Terreno Difícil and never provokes
opportunity attacks. When you force Mover a alvo into damaging
terrain or into terrain that produces an Efeito, they are affected as if they
had moved into it willingly.
```

```
Terreno Difícil
A Fúria with Velocidade 6 takes the Avançar Ação de Movimento across
a field with Água and bushes that create Terreno Difícil
(indicated by the blue squares on the map). Each highlighted
path indicates how many squares of Movimento they must
use while moving through or avoiding difficulty terrain. Their
Movimento can’t exceed 6 squares.
```

```
High Chão
The Talento stands atop a 3-Quadrado-high tower, which is higher
than qualquer other criatura. They gain an Vantagem on all Poder rolls
made against their inimigos in the diagram. The Goblin Assassino
and Cão de Guerra Comando stand on structures that are 2 squares
high. They gain an Vantagem on Habilidade rolls against the Tático,
who is standing on the Chão, but not against the Talento.
```

```
Combate
```

Vertical
If a Movimento Forçado Efeito has the word “Vertical” in front of it, then
the Movimento Forçado can Mover a alvo up or down in addition to hor-
izontally. For example, if a Movimento Forçado Efeito says “Vertical Empurrar
5,” then a criatura targeted by the Efeito can be pushed up to 5 squares
in qualquer Direção, as long as the Movimento Forçado is a straight Linha.

If a criatura who can’t Voar is left in midair at the end of a Vertical forced
Mover, they fall. Movimento Forçado made against a criatura who is flying
is always a Vertical forced Mover, whether or not the Efeito specifies it.

Though you can’t freely Empurrar, Puxar, or Deslizar a alvo up and down unless
that Movimento Forçado specifies “Vertical,” you can Mover them along a
physical slope such as a hill or staircase. For a alvo to be force moved
along a slope, each Quadrado of the slope can be no more than 1 Quadrado
higher or lower than the previous Quadrado.

Big Versus Little
When a larger criatura force moves a smaller alvo with a Corpo-a-corpo
Arma Habilidade, the Distância of the Movimento Forçado is increased by 1.
If a smaller criatura force moves a larger alvo with a Corpo-a-corpo Arma
Habilidade, the Distância doesn’t change.

Slamming into criaturas
When you force Mover a criatura into another criatura, the Movimento
ends and both criaturas take 1 dano for each Quadrado remaining in
the first criatura’s Movimento Forçado. You can also force Mover an objeto
into a criatura. The objeto’s Movimento ends, and the criatura takes 1
dano for each Quadrado remaining in the objeto’s Movimento Forçado.

```
It’s possible to Mover a criatura or objeto of a larger Tamanho into several
criaturas of a smaller Tamanho at the same time. When this happens, the
larger criatura in the collision takes dano only once, not once for
each smaller criatura they slam into.
```

```
If a criatura is killed by dano from an Habilidade or Efeito that also
force moves them, a second criatura they are slammed into still takes
dano unless the Diretor deems otherwise.
You can force Mover another criatura into yourself with a Puxar or a Deslizar.
```

```
Slamming Into criaturas
The Nulo slides a Cão de Guerra Comando 5 squares. The Nulo force
moves the Comando 1 Quadrado and then slams them into
another Adjacente Comando. The Movimento Forçado ends, and
both commandos take 4 dano, since the Movimento Forçado
still had 4 squares remaining when the commandos collided.
```

```
Movimento Forçado
The Fúria pushes a Cão de Guerra Comando 2 squares. The Censurador
pulls a Comando 2 squares. The Elementalista slides a
Comando 2 squares. Each Comando can end up anywhere
in the indicated Área of their Movimento Forçado on the diagram.
```

```
Vertical Movimento Forçado
The Talento verically slides the Goblin Corta-Espinhas 3 squares up
into the Ar and off of a cliff. The Goblin falls 5 squares, taking 10
dano and landing Derrubado from the fall.
```

```
Multitarget Abilities and Movimento Forçado
Some criaturas can force Mover multiple criaturas or objetos
with a single Habilidade. Unless the Habilidade specifies otherwise, the
criatura using the Habilidade determines the Ordem in which the
alvos are force moved. The criatura should select each alvo
individually and complete their Movimento Forçado before force
moving the next alvo affected.
```

Draw Steel

```
Slamming Into objetos
When a criatura force moves a alvo into a stationary objeto that is
the alvo’s Tamanho or larger and the objeto doesn’t break (see below), the
Movimento ends and the alvo takes 2 dano plus 1 dano for each
Quadrado remaining in their Movimento Forçado.
If you force Mover a criatura downward into an objeto that doesn’t
break (including the Chão), they also take Caindo dano as if they
had fallen the Distância force moved and their Agilidade score was 0 (see
Caindo above).
```

```
Arremesável Through objetos
When you Mover a criatura into a Mundano objeto, the objeto can break
depending on how many squares of Movimento Forçado remain. The cost
of being slammed into an objeto is tied to the dano a alvo takes for
being hurled through it:
¥ It costs 1 remaining Quadrado of Movimento Forçado to destroy 1 Quadrado
of glass. The criatura moved takes 3 dano.
¥ It costs 3 remaining squares of Movimento Forçado to destroy 1 Quadrado
of wood. The criatura moved takes 5 dano.
¥ It costs 6 remaining squares of Movimento Forçado to destroy 1 Quadrado
of Pedra. The criatura moved takes 8 dano.
¥ It costs 9 remaining squares of Movimento Forçado to destroy 1 Quadrado
of metal. The criatura moved takes 11 dano.
```

```
If qualquer Movimento Forçado remains after the objeto is destroyed, you can
continue to Mover the criatura who destroyed the objeto.
```

```
Forced Into a Fall
If you can’t Voar and are force moved across an Receptivo space that would
cause you to fall, such as being pushed over the Vantagem of a cliff, you
continue moving the total Distância you were moved first. If you are still
in a position to fall when the foced Movimento ends, you fall.
```

```
Estabilidade
Each criatura has a Estabilidade that allows them to resist forced
Movimento. When a criatura is force moved, they can reduce that
Movimento up to a number of squares equal to their Estabilidade. Heroes
start with Estabilidade 0 and can increase their Estabilidade through Linhagem,
Classe, and kit options.
A criatura’s Estabilidade can’t be less than 0, even when reduced
by a Penalidade.
```

```
“When a criatura Moves ...”
Certain abilities and effects Gatilho when a criatura moves into a
particular Área. Movimento Forçado triggers these options unless
otherwise noted, including an Efeito stating that a criatura must
willingly Mover to Gatilho it.
```

```
Morte Effects and Movimento Forçado
Some criaturas have traits or abilities that Gatilho when they die or
are reduced to 0 Vigor. If such a criatura is reduced to 0 Vigor by
dano from an Habilidade or Efeito that also force moves them, the forced
Movimento takes place before the triggered Efeito.
```

Mover Actions

```
A Ação de Movimento allows a criatura to Mover around the battlefield.
Sometimes you’ll already be exactly where you want to be so that you
don’t need to use a Ação de Movimento on your Turno. That’s okay! The decision
to not Mover is just as tactical as the decision to Mover.
```

```
Avançar
When a criatura takes the Avançar Ação de Movimento, they Mover a number
of squares up to their Velocidade. They can break up this Movimento with
their Manobra and Ação Principal however they wish.
```

**Retirar-se**

```
When a criatura takes the Retirar-se Ação de Movimento, they can Ajustar-se 1
Quadrado. Certain Classe features, kits, and other rules allow a criatura
to Ajustar-se more than 1 Quadrado when they Retirar-se. A criatura who
does so can break up their Ajustar-se with their Manobra and Ação Principal
however they wish.
```

```
Montar
A criatura can take the Montar Ação de Movimento only while mounted on
another criatura (see Mounted Combate below). When a criatura
takes the Montar Ação de Movimento, they cause their Montaria to Mover up to the
Montaria’s Velocidade, taking the rider with them. Alternatively, a criatura can
use the Montar Ação de Movimento to have their Montaria use the Retirar-se Mover
action as a Reação Livre. A criatura can use the Montar Ação de Movimento
only once per Ronda. A mounted criatura can only have this Mover
action applied to them once per Ronda. This Movimento can be broken
up with the rider’s Manobra and Ação Principal however they wish.
```

```
Arremesável Through objetos
The Nulo slides a Cão de Guerra Comando 5 squares. The Nulo force
moves the Comando 1 Quadrado and then slams them into a
thick wooden Parede. The Nulo forces the Comando through the
first Quadrado of the Parede by using 3 squares of Movimento Forçado,
resulting in the Comando taking 5 dano. The Comando
still has 1 Quadrado of Movimento Forçado left, so they are pushed
into the next Quadrado of the Parede, which doesn’t break but does
result in the Comando’s forced moment ending and them
taking another 3 dano: 1 for the Quadrado of Movimento Forçado
leftover and 2 for colliding with an objeto.
```

```
Tracking objeto Forced-Movimento dano
At the Diretor’s discretion, Mundano objetos that are force
moved into criaturas or other objetos take dano as if they
were criaturas. Sturdy objetos can take dano as follows
before they are destroyed:
¥ Wood objeto: 3 dano for each Quadrado it occupies
¥ Pedra objeto: 6 dano for each Quadrado it occupies
¥ Metal objeto: 9 dano for each Quadrado it occupies
More fragile objetos are destroyed after taking qualquer dano.
```

```
Combate
```

Maneuvers

A Manobra typically involves less Foco and exertion than a Ação Principal
(see below). It can be an opportunity to Mover other criaturas, drink a
potion, or undertake similar activities.

Sometimes you Músculo not have anything you can do with your Manobra.
That’s totally fine! Often, the best thing to do on your Turno is take a main
action and Mover on.

**Auxiliar Ataque**

A criatura who uses the Auxiliar Ataque Manobra chooses an inimigo Adjacente
to them. The next Habilidade roll an aliado makes against that inimigo before the
start of the aiding criatura’s next Turno gains an Vantagem.

**Recuperar Fôlego**

A criatura who uses the Recuperar Fôlego Manobra spends a Recuperação and
regains Vigor equal to their Recuperação value. (See below for Vigor. See
Recoveries in Chapter 1: The Basics.)

A criatura who is Morrendo (see Morrendo and Morte in Vigor below) can’t
use the Recuperar Fôlego Manobra, but other criaturas can help them Gastar
Recoveries in other ways.

**Escapar Agarrão**

A criatura who is Agarrado by another criatura, an objeto, or an Efeito (see
Agarrar below) can attempt to escape by using the following Habilidade.

```
Escapar Agarrão
— Manobra
e Personagem x Personagem
```

```
Poder Roll + Músculo or Agilidade :
á No Efeito.
é You can escape the Agarrar, but if you do, a criatura who has you
Agarrado can make a Corpo-a-corpo Golpe Simples against you before you
are no longer Agarrado.
í You are no longer Agarrado.
Efeito: You take a Desvantagem on this Manobra if your Tamanho is smaller than
the Tamanho of the criatura, objeto, or Efeito that has you Agarrado.
```

See Conditions in Chapter 5: Classes for information on the
Agarrado Condição.

**Agarrar**

A criatura tentando to keep a foe close and locked down can attempt to
Agarrar a criatura using the following Habilidade.

```
Agarrar
Corpo-a-corpo, Arma Manobra
e Corpo-a-corpo 1 x um criatura
```

```
Poder Roll + Músculo :
á No Efeito.
é You can Agarrar the alvo, but if you do, the alvo can make a
Corpo-a-corpo Golpe Simples against you before they are Agarrado.
í The alvo is Agarrado by you.
Efeito: You can usually alvo only criaturas of your Tamanho or smaller.
If your Músculo score is 2 or higher, you can alvo qualquer criatura with a
Tamanho equal to or less than your Músculo score.
```

Unless otherwise indicated, a criatura can Agarrar only um criatura at a time.

See Conditions in Chapter 5: Classes for information on the
Agarrado Condição.

```
Esconder-se
Using the Esconder-se Manobra, a criatura attempts to Esconder-se from other
criaturas who aren’t observing them while they have Cobertura or
Encobrimento. See Esconder-se and Furtivo in Chapter 9: Tests for full details.
```

```
Empurrar
A criatura wanting to Empurrar an Adjacente criatura away from them can
attempt to shove that criatura using the following Habilidade.
```

```
Empurrar
Corpo-a-corpo, Arma Manobra
e Corpo-a-corpo 1 x 1 criatura
```

```
Poder Roll + M ight:
á Empurrar 1
é Empurrar 2
í Empurrar 3
Efeito: You can usually alvo only criaturas of your Tamanho or smaller.
If your Músculo score is 2 or higher, you can alvo qualquer criatura with a
Tamanho equal to or less than your Músculo score.
```

```
Hiding
To become Escondida, the Sombra can’t be observed by the Guerra
dog Crucibita, so they must get out of the Crucibita’s Linha of
Efeito. In this situation, the Sombra could do this by moving to
put a Parede between them and the Crucibita or moving up onto
a roof.
```

Draw Steel

```
Make or Auxiliar um Teste
Many tests are maneuvers if made durante o Combate. Searching a chest with
a Razão Teste, picking a door’s lock with an Agilidade Teste, or lifting a
portcullis with a Músculo Teste would all be maneuvers. Assisting a Teste is
also a Manobra durante o Combate (see Auxiliar um Teste in Chapter 9: Tests).
```

```
Complex or time-consuming tests Músculo require a Ação Principal if
made durante o Combate—or could take so long that they can’t be made during
Combate at all. Other tests that take no time at all, such as a Razão Teste
to Recolher lore about mummies, are usually free maneuvers durante o Combate.
The Diretor has the final say regarding which tests can be made
as maneuvers.
```

```
Procurar Criaturas Escondidas
The Procurar Criaturas Escondidas Manobra allows a criatura to
attempt to locate criaturas Escondida from them (see Esconder-se and Furtivo in
Chapter 9: Tests).
```

**Levantar**

```
A criatura can use the Levantar Manobra to Levantar if they are
Derrubado, ending that Condição. Alternatively, they can use this Manobra
to make a willing Adjacente Derrubado criatura Levantar.
```

```
Usar Consumível
Unless otherwise noted in its description, a criatura can Ativar
a Consumível Tesouro such as a potion with the Usar Consumível
Manobra. A criatura can use this Manobra to administer a
Consumível Tesouro that benefits the user either to themself or to a
willing Adjacente criatura. See Consumables in Chapter 13: Rewards.
```

Main Actions

```
When you take a Ação Principal, you most often do so to use a unique
Habilidade granted by your Classe, kit, or a Tesouro (see Abilities in
Chapter 5: Classes). These abilities represent the most unique, flavorful,
and impactful things you can do with your Ação Principal.
You can also use your Ação Principal to catch your Sopro, help another
criatura regain Vigor, Investir into battle, Defensor yourself, or make a
Golpe Simples.
```

```
You can convert your Ação Principal into a Manobra or a Ação de Movimento,
allowing you to take dois maneuvers or Mover actions on your Turno.
```

```
Investir
When a criatura takes the Investir Ação Principal, they Mover up to their
Velocidade in a straight Linha, then make a Corpo-a-corpo Golpe Simples (see Free Strikes
below) against a alvo when they end their Mover. If the criatura has an
Habilidade with the Investir Palavra-Chave, they can use that Habilidade against the
alvo instead of a Golpe Simples.
```

```
A criatura can’t Mover through Terreno Difícil or Ajustar-se when they
Investir. They can Voar or Escavar as part of the Investir Ação Principal if they
have that Movimento available to them, but they can’t Escalar or Nadar
while charging unless they can automatically use that Movimento
at full Velocidade.
```

```
Defensor
When a criatura takes the Defensor Ação Principal, Habilidade rolls made
against them have a double Desvantagem até o início do seu próximo turno.
Additionally, you have a double Vantagem on tests when called for to resist
environmental effects or a criatura’s traits or abilities. A criatura gains
no Benefício from this action while another criatura is Provocado by them
(see Conditions in Chapter 5: Classes).
```

**Golpe Simples**

```
A criatura can use this Ação Principal to make a Golpe Simples (see Free
Strikes below). Most of the time, you’ll want to use the more impactful
main actions granted by your Classe, kit, or other Recurso, just as the
Diretor will use the main actions in a criatura’s Ficha de Criatura, but free
strikes are available for when all else fails. For instance, a Fúria who has
no other options for À Distância strikes Músculo use the À Distância Arma Free
Golpe Habilidade with an improvised Arma when battling a flying foe.
```

```
Curar
A criatura who uses the Curar Ação Principal employs medicine or
inspiring words to make an Adjacente criatura feel better and stay in
the fight. The alvo criatura can Gastar a Recuperação to regain Vigor,
or can make a Teste de Resistência against um Efeito they are suffering that is
ended by a Teste de Resistência.
```

```
Combate
```

Free Strikes

Every criatura can use a Golpe Simples Habilidade as a Ação Principal on their
Turno, though doing so typically isn’t the most effective choice. Most of
the time, you’ll use free strikes when the rules call for it. Specific rules
let you use free strikes as part of an action that allows you to also do
something else impactful, such as how the Investir Ação Principal lets you
Mover and use a Corpo-a-corpo Golpe Simples in um Ação Principal (see Investir above).

Many rules and abilities allow heroes to make free strikes when it
isn’t their Turno, such as the Tático’s Cobertura Habilidade. As well, all
characters can make an Ataque de Oportunidade Golpe Simples.

**Granted Abilities**

Some abilities, such as the Tático’s Golpe Now or I’ll Receptivo and
You’ll Close abilities, allow another criatura to use a signature Habilidade
or heroic Habilidade when it isn’t their Turno. Unless otherwise stated, a
criatura can always use a Golpe Simples instead of a granted signature
Habilidade or heroic Habilidade.

**Opportunity Attacks**

Whenever a criatura has an inimigo Adjacente to them and the inimigo
willingly moves to a space that isn’t Adjacente to the criatura without
shifting, the criatura can take advantage of that Movimento to quickly
make a Corpo-a-corpo Golpe Simples against the inimigo as a Reação Livre.
This is called an Ataque de Oportunidade.

If a criatura has a Desvantagem or double Desvantagem on the Poder roll against the
inimigo, they can’t make an Ataque de Oportunidade.

**Standard Free Strikes**

Every Herói has dois standard Golpe Simples abilities available to them. Your
Classe Músculo give you additional Golpe Simples options, and your kit can
improve the standard options (see Chapter 6: Kits).

A Corpo-a-corpo Arma Golpe Simples is a Corpo-a-corpo Golpe made with an unarmed
Golpe or an improvised Arma. A À Distância Arma Golpe Simples is a À Distância
Golpe made with an improvised Arma. At the Diretor’s discretion,
the dano Tipo of an improvised Arma can change based on the
objeto used. For example, if you use a Queimando torch as an improvised
Arma, it could deal Fogo dano when used for a Golpe Simples.

```
Corpo-a-corpo Arma Golpe Simples
Investir, Corpo-a-corpo, Golpe, Arma Ação Principal
e Corpo-a-corpo 1 x um criatura or objeto
```

```
Poder Roll + Músculo or Agilidade:
á 2 + M or A dano
é 5 + M or A dano
í 7 + M or A dano
```

```
À Distância Arma Golpe Simples
À Distância, Golpe, Arma Ação Principal
e À Distância 5 x um criatura or objeto
```

```
Poder Roll + Músculo or Agilidade:
á 2 + M or A dano
é 4 + M or A dano
í 6 + M or A dano
```

```
Opportunity Attacks
The Tático can’t make qualquer opportunity attacks against
these Adjacente Cães de Guerra as they Mover. Despite moving, the
Comando never stops being Adjacente to the Tático, and the
Crucibita shifts away instead of moving.
```

```
Opportunity Attacks: Moving Out
A Cão de Guerra Crucibita moves out of a space that is Adjacente to the
Tático and into a space that isn’t Adjacente. The Tático can
make an Ataque de Oportunidade against the Crucibita.
```

```
Opportunity Attacks: Moving With Banes
The Cão de Guerra eviservite has a Desvantagem on strikes against the
Adjacente Censurador, so the Censurador can freely Mover away from the
evisercite without worrying about the Cão de Guerra making an
Ataque de Oportunidade.
```

Draw Steel

```
Flanqueando
When you and um or more aliados are Adjacente to the same inimigo and
on opposite sides of the inimigo, you are Flanqueando that inimigo. While
Flanqueando an inimigo, you gain an Vantagem on Corpo-a-corpo strikes against them.
```

```
If you’re unsure whether your Herói and an aliado are Flanqueando a foe,
imagine a Linha extending from the center of your space to the center of
your aliado’s space. If that Linha passes through opposite sides or corners of
the inimigo’s space, then you and your aliado are Flanqueando the inimigo.
You must have Linha of Efeito to the inimigo and be able to take triggered
actions to gain or grant the Flanqueando Benefício.
```

```
Flanqueando
The tacitician flanks the Cão de Guerra Amalgamita with the
Elementalista and Talento, since they are on directly opposite
sides of their inimigo. No heroes flank the other Amalgamita.
The Censurador, using an Habilidade with a Distância of Corpo-a-corpo 2, isn’t
Adjacente to the Amalgamita and so can’t flank with the Sombra.
The Fúria and Nulo aren’t on directly opposite sides of the
Amalgamita, and so they aren’t Flanqueando their inimigo either.
```

```
Flanqueando
The Censurador flanks the Cão de Guerra Comando with the Fúria,
since they are on directly opposite sides of their inimigo. The
Trovador isn’t Flanqueando the criatura with the Censurador though,
since they aren’t on directly opposite sides. The Sombra can’t
flank the Crucibita with the Conduíta because the Conduíta is
Atordoado, which prevents them from taking triggered actions.
```

```
Cobertura
The Cão de Guerra Comando has Cobertura against a Golpe from the
tacitician, since a low Parede between them covers half of the
Comando’s body. The tacitician can’t attack the Crucibita,
since much higher walls completely block the Crucibita’s body,
and therefore the tacitician does not have Linha of Efeito to the
Crucibita.
```

Cobertura

```
When you have Linha of Efeito to a criatura or objeto but that alvo has
at least half their form blocked by a solid objeto such as a tree, Parede, or
overturned table, the alvo has Cobertura. You take a Desvantagem on dano-deal-
ing abilities used against criaturas or objetos that have Cobertura from you.
```

Encobrimento

```
Darkness, Névoa, invisibility Magia, and qualquer other Efeito that fully obscures
a criatura or objeto but doesn’t protect their physical form grants that
criatura or objeto Encobrimento. Even if you have Linha of Efeito to such
a alvo, a criatura or objeto has Encobrimento from you if you can’t see
or otherwise observe them. You can alvo a criatura or objeto with
Encobrimento using a Golpe, provided they aren’t Escondida (see Esconder-se
and Furtivo in Chapter 9: Tests). However, strikes against such alvos
take a Desvantagem.
```

**Invisível criaturas**

```
Invisível criaturas always have Encobrimento from other criaturas. If an
Invisível criatura isn’t Escondida, they can still be targeted by abilities. The
Teste made to find a Escondida criatura who is Invisível takes a Desvantagem.
```

```
Encobrimento
The Tático is shrouded in Névoa, which provides them with
Encobrimento against a Golpe from the Cão de Guerra Crucibita. The
Crucibita’s Golpe takes a Desvantagem as a result.
```

```
Combate
```

```
Vigor
Your Herói’s survivability is represented by your Vigor. Think of
Vigor as a combination of a criatura’s physical vitality and their
overall energy for dodging and resisting incoming blows, spells, and
other violence. It’s not that every instance of dano deals a Sangrando
wound to you, but that each um chips away at your Habilidade to fight
effectively. um attack Músculo make you sweat as you Pulo back to
avoid an arrow, while another Músculo graze your elbow with a dagger
nick, leaving a dull, distracting pain. Eventually, this Drenante of energy
leaves you Receptivo for bigger blows that can truly harm your body—or
possibly kill you.
```

```
After qualquer dano you take is reduced by Imunidade a Dano or other
effects, your Vigor is reduced by an amount equal to the remaining
dano. Some effects can also reduce your Vigor maximum, limiting
the amount of Vigor you can regain.
```

```
Recoveries and Recuperação Value
Each Herói has a number of Recoveries determined by their Classe. A
Herói also has a Recuperação value that equals um-third of their Vigor
maximum, rounded down. When you use the Recuperar Fôlego Manobra
durante o Combate (see Maneuvers above), you Gastar a Recuperação and regain
Vigor equal to your Recuperação value. fora de Combate, you can
Gastar as many Recoveries as you have remaining. Some abilities, items,
and other effects allow you to Gastar a Recuperação to regain Vigor
equal to your Recuperação value plus a little extra (as described by the
Efeito), or to regain Vigor without spending a Recuperação.
```

dano

Strikes, Área attacks, environmental effects, and other hazards can all
deal dano to the heroes and their foes. Whenever a criatura takes
dano, they reduce their Vigor (see below) by an amount equal to
the dano taken.

**dano Types**

Typical dano, such as that caused by weapons, Caindo, traps, and
monstrous Garras, has no Tipo associated with it. That’s because for
most criaturas, there’s no difference in the amount of harm caused by
being run through with a pike, dropped from a height onto a Pedra floor,
slashed by a pendulum scythe, or skewered on a Minotauro’s horns.

However, when it comes to Elemental and Sobrenatural dano
sources, some criaturas Músculo have an immunity or weakness to that
dano. As such, abilities and effects note when they deal qualquer of the
following dano types: Ácido, Frio, Corrupção, Fogo, Sagrado, Elétrico,
Veneno, Psíquico, or Sônico.

Imunidade a Dano
Imunidade a Dano means that a criatura can ignore some or all of the
dano they would usually take from certain attacks or effects.

Imunidade a Dano Músculo have a dano Tipo associated with it,
expressed as “[dano Tipo] immunity.” Imunidade a Dano often has a
value associated with it, so that um criatura’s Ficha de Criatura notes “dano
immunity 5” (representing immunity to all dano), while another
criatura has “Elétrico immunity 5.” Whenever a alvo with dano
immunity takes dano of the indicated Tipo, they can reduce the
dano by the value of the immunity (to a minimum of 0 dano). If
the value of the immunity is “all,” then the alvo ignores all dano of
the indicated Tipo.

Imunidade a Dano should be the last thing applied when calculating
dano. For instance, if your Herói has Fogo immunity 5 and takes 8 Fogo
dano, they take 3 dano. But if an aliado first halved the dano with
a Reação, your Herói would take 4 dano before immunity is
applied, with immunity then reducing the dano to 0.

If multiple dano immunities apply to a source of dano, only the
immunity with the highest value applies. For instance, a criatura with
Imunidade a Dano 5 and Fogo immunity 10 who takes 12 Fogo dano
reduces the dano by 10 points.

Fraqueza a Dano
Fraqueza a Dano works like Imunidade a Dano, except that criaturas
take extra dano whenever they take dano of the indicated
Tipo. For instance, if a criatura has Fogo weakness 5 and is dealt 10 Fogo
dano, they take 15 Fogo dano instead.

A criatura who has “Fraqueza a Dano X” with no specific Tipo or
Palavra-Chave indicated has weakness of the indicated amount when they
take dano of qualquer Tipo.

If a criatura has both Imunidade a Dano and Fraqueza a Dano for a
source of dano, apply the weakness first, then the immunity.

If multiple dano weaknesses apply to a source of dano, only the
weakness with the highest value applies.

Draw Steel

```
Ofegante
Your Ofegante value equals half your Vigor maximum. When your
Vigor is equal to or less than your Ofegante value, you are Ofegante.
Although being Ofegante has no effects on its own, certain Linhagem,
Classe, item, Título, and Monstro abilities affect Ofegante criaturas.
```

```
You can tell when other criaturas are Ofegante and vice versa.
```

```
Morrendo and Morte
When your Vigor is 0 or lower, you are Morrendo. While Morrendo, you
can’t use the Recuperar Fôlego Manobra durante o Combate. Additionally, you are
Sangrando, and this instance of the Condição can’t be negated or removed
in qualquer way until you are no longer Morrendo. While you are Morrendo, you can
still act, your aliados can help you Gastar Recoveries durante o Combate, and you
can Gastar Recoveries out of Combate as usual.
```

```
While your Vigor is lower than 0, if it reaches the negative of your
Ofegante value, you die. When you die, you can’t be brought back to
Vida without the use of a Especial powerful item, such as a Scroll of
Resurrection.
```

```
Diretor-Controlled criaturas
In most circumstances, Diretor-controlled criaturas die or are
destroyed when their Vigor drops to 0.
```

```
No Recoveries
Diretor-controlled criaturas don’t have Recoveries or a Recuperação value.
qualquer such criaturas who regain Vigor during a battle do so by way of
a Especial item or an Habilidade in their Ficha de Criatura. However, there are times
when a Herói Músculo wish to use an Habilidade that allows another criatura
to Gastar a Recuperação or to regain Vigor equal to their Recuperação value
on an injured NPC. In such cases, a Diretor-controlled criatura regains
Vigor equal to um-third of their Vigor maximum.
```

**Knocking criaturas Out**

```
If you dano a criatura with an Habilidade that would kill them, you can
choose to instead knock them Inconsciente. If a criatura takes dano
while Inconsciente in this way, they die.
Diretor-controlled criaturas remain Inconsciente for 1 hour if no um
does anything to wake them. They then gain 1 Vigor and are no
longer Inconsciente.
```

```
Heroes remain Inconsciente for 1 hour if no um does anything to
wake them. After 1 hour, they can Gastar a Recuperação and are no longer
Inconsciente. If the Herói has no Recoveries left, they can’t wake up until
they finish a Descanso.
```

```
Inconsciente
While you are Inconsciente, you can’t take main actions, maneuvers,
triggered actions, free triggered actions, or free maneuvers; your
Velocidade is 0; you are unaware of your surroundings; and you are Derrubado.
Habilidade rolls against you have a double Vantagem. If you wake up from being
Inconsciente, you can Levantar from Derrubado as a Manobra Livre.
```

```
Temporary Vigor
Some abilities, treasures, and other effects grant a criatura temporary
Vigor. Temporary Vigor shouldn’t be included in a criatura’s
Vigor total when figuring out a criatura’s Recuperação value or Ofegante
value. If you have temporary Vigor while Ofegante, Morrendo, or dead, the
temporary Vigor doesn’t change those states.
```

```
Whenever you take dano while you have temporary Vigor, the
temporary Vigor decreases first, and qualquer leftover dano is applied
to your Vigor as usual. For instance, if you have 10 temporary
Vigor and take 16 dano, you lose the temporary Vigor and then
lose another 6 Vigor.
There is no maximum to how much temporary Vigor you can
have. Regaining Vigor can’t restore temporary Vigor. If you have
temporary Vigor and then gain more temporary Vigor, you
get whichever amount of temporary Vigor is greater, rather than
adding the dois pools together. For instance, if an Habilidade grants you 10
temporary Vigor when you already have 5, you have 10 temporary
Vigor, not 15.
```

```
Unless otherwise indicated, temporary Vigor disappears at the end
of an Encontro.
```

```
objeto Vigor
Mundano objetos in the game have Vigor based on the material
they’re made of. When an objeto’s Vigor is reduced to 0, the objeto
is destroyed. objetos have Veneno immunity all and Psíquico immunity
all, though the Diretor can remove um or both of these immunities in
the case of living objetos, such as plants. A Tamanho 1 objeto or 1 Quadrado of a
larger objeto made of common materials has Vigor as follows:
```

```
¥ Glass: 1 Vigor
¥ Wood: 3 Vigor
¥ Pedra: 6 Vigor
¥ Metal: 9 Vigor
The Diretor can decide that a well-made or poorly made objeto has
more or less Vigor. Destroying a Sobrenatural objeto often (but not
always) requires a specific quest, such as throwing a Magia ring back
into the volcano where it was forged.
```

Underwater Combate

```
If a criatura is fully submerged in Água, they have Fogo immunity 5 and
Elétrico weakness 5. If they can’t automatically Nadar at full Velocidade
while moving, their Poder rolls take a Desvantagem.
```

```
Sufocando
During Combate or under similarly stressful circumstances, you can hold
your Sopro for a number of Combate rounds equal to your Músculo score
(minimum 1 Ronda). At the end of each Combate Ronda after that, you
take 1d6 dano while holding your Sopro.
```

```
Out of Combate, you can hold your Sopro for a number of minutes equal
to your Músculo score. Being unable to breathe after that time counts as a
stressful Condição, causing you to run out of Ar as above.
```

```
Combate
```

Mounted Combate

A willing criatura with the Montaria role (see criatura Roles in
_Draw Steel: Monsters_ ) can serve as your Montaria as long as their Tamanho
is greater than yours. You can Escalar onto your Montaria freely (see
Escalador Other criaturas above). You determine which space you
occupy. While mounted, you can take the Montar Ação de Movimento, but a
Montaria can only be ridden this way once per Ronda. Both Montaria and
rider each take a Turno during Combate.

If a criatura riding a Montaria is force moved, they are knocked off
the Montaria and must Fazer um Teste to determine how they land (see
Escalador Other criaturas). If a Montaria is force moved, they carry qualquer
riders with them. Riders and mounts Teleportar-se separately.

If your Montaria dies, they fall Derrubado, and you fall off them and land Derrubado
in the nearest quadrado desocupado of your choice.

End of Combate

At the end of Combate, the Diretor determines if the heroes earn qualquer
Victories. qualquer Efeito or Condição on you that you suffered during
Combate (except for being Ofegante, Inconsciente, or Morrendo) ends if
you want it to.

**How Combate Ends**

The Diretor determines when a Combate Encontro is over. While some
battles—especially showdowns with important villains—can be about
a fight to the bitter end, many other encounters can become a tedious
slog if the heroes need to fight until every last inimigo’s Vigor is
reduced to 0.

To avoid a battle dragging, the Diretor can set objectives when they
build the Encontro. Once the heroes achieve those objectives, or if
it becomes Tempo Limpo that they can win the fight with minimal effort, the
Diretor can end the Encontro. They Músculo do so by calling “Cut!” like
a film Diretor, or they can use some other phrase or indicator.

When the Diretor ends Combate this way, the jogadores typically choose
how the battle ends by narrating a dramatic finish. Or in rarer cases
when the heroes achieve a major Objetivo that sets off a story-defin-
ing event, the Diretor narrates the end of the battle with a positive
outcome for the jogadores, called an event ending (see below).

**Objetivo Endings**

While planning a Combate Encontro, the Diretor can set um or more
objectives the heroes can achieve to end the Encontro without
dropping every last foe. Some broad categories of objectives are
described in this section, but the Diretor should feel free to create their
own. As well, Directors can always end Combate anytime it becomes
Tempo Limpo that the heroes are going to win an Encontro with minimal effort,
even if they haven’t achieved all the objectives.

Each of the Objetivo endings in this section is explored in detail—
including looking at Monstro roles, map advice, Sucesso conditions, and
more—in the Introduction section of _Draw Steel: Monsters_.

Diminish Numbers
The simplest Combate Encontro Objetivo is almost always “defeat them
before they defeat us.” Though the heroes don’t have to kill every last
inimigo in this Tipo of Encontro, winning the day requires that they Empurrar
their opponents to the point where they are broken, flee, or surrender.

```
Defeat a Specific Foe
An Encontro built around defeating a specific foe includes um or
more of the heroes’ inimigos commanding the rest, such as a hobgoblin
Lorde de Sangue Conduzindo a group of mercenaries, or um or more particularly
powerful foes among a group of weaker ones, such as a pair of tusker
demons in a Gnoll Guerra band. Because these more-powerful inimigos are
the stars of the Encontro, if only Fraca foes are left once the stars are
gone, the battle loses its Desafio and it’s time to wrap it up. It makes
sense for those weaker foes to flee or surrender once their strongest
aliados have gone down.
```

```
Get the Thing!
Classic heroic fantasy is full of important objetos that the heroes must
protect from the forces of evil: Magia rings, royal birth certificates,
Dragão eggs, and the like. Heroes often find themselves at violent odds
with their inimigos as they race to collect a valuable or important item
from a guarded temple or castle, or when they need to steal the item
from a group of inimigos already in possession of it.
Objectives in this category work well when paired with other
objectives, such as defeating a specific foe. For instance, the heroes must
steal a ledger containing a record of Criminoso activity from an Supermente
and her lackeys. However, even if they obtain the ledger, the battle
won’t be over until they also defeat the Supermente, who won’t let the
book go without a fight!
```

Draw Steel

```
Destroy the Thing!
Combate doesn’t always have to be about destroying your inimigos.
Sometimes it’s about destroying their stuff! Queimando a Pirata Capitão’s
vessel, closing a portal to the Abissal Wasteland before it lets in an
army of demons, or shutting down a massive kobold Armadilha made of
Lâminas Giratórias could so hamper the heroes’ foes that the battle is no
longer worth fighting once the dano is done.
```

```
Save Another
No um earns the mantle of Herói without saving a few lives. Sometimes
the point of an Encontro isn’t to kill, but to save as many folks as you
can. If the heroes rescue powerful aliados from the clutches of their foes
during Combate, the added strength of those aliados Músculo be enough
to make the remainder of the Encontro trivial. When you and your
companions save a Grifo from a crew of poachers, the hunters become
the ... well, you know the rest.
```

```
Escort
Surprising as it may seem, sometimes the Destino of the mission doesn’t
rest on the heroes’ shoulders at all! Sometimes it rests on the shoulders
of someone standing next to the heroes. The heroes’ job is to keep this
important person safe as they travel to a specific destination.
Not every escort Encontro is on behalf of a wise or mighty aliado.
Sometimes the heroes are tasked with protecting a helpless or even an
actively troublesome criatura, such as a hapless Nobre or a wayward
child. They Músculo even have to protect a bulky or inconvenient
inanimate objeto. Whatever the case, the inimigos just keep coming
until the heroes get their Investir to their destination.
```

```
Hold Them Off
Sometimes the heroes just need to buy time. They Músculo need to
battle a conquering tyrant’s army to allow innocent villagers time to
escape. They Músculo need to hold off Ondulante after Ondulante of zombies while
a group of priests completes a ritual to lay the Morto-Vivo to rest for good.
To achieve this Objetivo, the heroes need to stay alive and protect a
particular position for a number of rounds determined by you.
```

```
Assault the Defenses
The inimigo holds a strategically important position and the heroes
want it. The Encontro ends when the heroes secure the Objetivo
defensive location for themselves, even if there are more inimigos
outside it. Sometimes an Encontro with this Objetivo is part of a
combined Objetivo, as when heroes must first assault the defenses,
then hold that defensive position against counterattack.
```

```
Stop the Action
Sometimes Combate is complicated by the fact that the heroes need to
stop the villainous actions of their foes. It’s not enough to simply defeat
the warriors in a cult. The heroes must also stop the zealots’ archdev-
il-summoning ritual! Or it Músculo be that the heroes need to interrupt
a wedding and make sure an evil mage doesn’t marry the heir to the
throne. Despite Combate, the mage forces the ceremony to continue!
Objectives in this category have a timer associated with them. If the
heroes don’t achieve the Objetivo in a certain number of rounds, the
conditions of the battle could well change. For instance, if the cultists
summon the archdevil, defeating the Diabo suddenly becomes the
heroes’ new Objetivo!
```

```
Complete the Action
This Encontro Objetivo sees the characters charged with initiating
an event, performing a ritual, and so forth. For instance, if the heroes
are attempting to launch an airship while repelling a Invasor do Futuro
boarding party, the Encontro could be over the moment the heroes
manage to Ativar the vessel and take off with just a few time raiders
actually aboard.
```

```
Dramatic Finish
If the heroes are able to end a fight with a dramatic finish, the Diretor
assigns each Herói um or more of their remaining inimigos, then asks
that Herói’s jogador to describe how the Herói neutralizes that threat. The
Herói Músculo deliver a killing blow, knock their foe out, or let the inimigo
flee with their tail between their legs (literally or figuratively). If the
fight has more heroes than Diretor-controlled inimigos, the Diretor
can assign more than um Herói to an inimigo, then ask the jogadores
how their characters work together to bring that inimigo down. After
everyone gives a description, the battle ends.
```

**Event Ending**

```
If the Diretor calls the end of Combate when a specific Objetivo in
an Encontro is achieved, the event ending creates a big narrative
finish. The Diretor can pick a narrative Gatilho for an event ending
before an Encontro begins, or can come up with um on the Voar if that
makes more sense.
Event endings can Cobertura big scenarios such as the characters destroying
a dam to unleash a river upon their inimigos, or completing a ritual
that causes all the demons they’ve been battling to be sent back to the
Abissal Wasteland, accompanied by visual details. For example, if the
heroes are battling a necromancer who controls a Horda of zombies, the
Morto-Vivo Músculo all crumble to dust when the necromancer is defeated. If
the heroes destroy an eldritch machine sapping the land of its natural
energy, the Onda de Choque from the device’s destruction could vaporize the
cultists attempting to protect it.
```

```
Fleeing Foes
If you’ve played a fantasy RPG before, odds are you’ve had an
Encontro where you didn’t chase down every last fleeing
foe—and then um such foe Agarrado another bunch of evil
buddies and came back to ambush you. It takes only um
experience like this to create jogadores who promise, “No
survivors. No mercy!” whenever foes break ranks. Chasing
down every last foe can be fun once in a while, but it can easily
Turno a tactical Encontro into a slog.
Luckily, this is a heroic game. Although the Diretor can
surprise the jogadores with dramatic reveals and twisty-turny
stories, “Gotcha!” moments that make jogadores Desconfiado of
every fleeing bandit shouldn’t be part of those stories. If a
bandit is fleeing an Encontro, they’re running away to rethink
their Vida. If they’re going for help, the jogadores should get some
sense of that—for example, the bandit screaming at the top
of their lungs for help as they run toward their Líder’s tent.
That way, the jogadores can process what’s happening, and will
understand that stopping that fleeing bandit is part of the
Desafio of the Encontro.
```

Combate

```
Negociação
```

```
Chapter 11
```

# **Negociação**

Negociar dá aos heróis uma chance de conseguir o que querem sem combate... ou ao menos sem mais combate! Você pode negociar com um rei para obter apoio militar contra uma invasão demoníaca em um reino vizinho. Você pode tentar convencer uma líder de bandidos a parar de atacar caravanas de mercadores na estrada e, em vez disso, mirar em nobres leais a um tirano. Você pode tentar convencer um arquimago a permitir acesso à sua biblioteca secreta para pesquisar a localização de um machado matador-de-dragões. A Negociação cobre todos esses cenário e mais.

Pense na Negociação como aprender um novo sistema de combate, exploração ou investigação em um RPG. Este conjunto de regras oferece uma estrutura para interpretação. As regras de Negociação devem ser lidas tanto por jogadores quanto por Diretores, para que todos entendam as regras de Negociação. Se você nunca jogou um jogo com um sistema de Negociação dedicado como esse, você pode precisar passar por ele uma ou duas vezes antes de dominá-lo, assim como para aprender qualquer subconjunto de regras de um RPG. Se um jogador não tiver lido essas regras, o Diretor e os demais podem explicá-las durante sua primeira Negociação.

Negociação é uma estrutura para interpretar encontros importantes onde os heróis querem convencer um NPC a tomar certas ações, como emprestar um Artefato aos heróis ou perdoar um prisioneiro. Esta estrutura monitora o Interesse do NPC nos argumentos do herói e sua Paciência, para que o Diretor saiba o que o NPC está disposto a oferecer e quando é hora de encerrar a cena. Esta estrutura não deve substituir a interpretação (embora certamente possa ajudar se seu grupo não gosta dessa parte em RPGs). A estrutura está aqui para ajudar jogadores e Diretores a entenderem os mecanismos do vai e vem de uma conversa, além de dar algumas regras que podem tornar uma conversa de alto risco ainda mais dramática!

## Quando Negociar

Para que uma Negociação ocorra, um NPC precisa ter interesse em negociar com os heróis - mas também razões para não simplesmente aceitar o que eles propõem. Negociações só ocorrem quando o NPC tem essa tensão interna entre interesse e relutância. Por exemplo, se os personagens pedem ao rei que envie seu exército para lutar contra uma invasão demoníaca num reino vizinho, o rei precisa estar dividido. Ele quer deter a invasão, mas também não quer arriscar a vida de seus soldados defendendo um reino estrangeiro, deixando os seus próprios súditos desprotegidos. Se os heróis quiserem a ajuda desse exército, eles terão que negociar.

Não se espera que os heróis usem essas regras toda vez que tentarem convencer um NPC. Por exemplo, se um herói quer que um cultista capturado dê informações sobre o líder do culto, um Teste de Presença usando Mentir ou um Teste de Músculo com Intimidar provavelmente bastam. Um personagem que quiser flertar com o alquimista local para conseguir uma Poção de Cura grátis provavelmente só precisa de um Teste de Presença com a Perícia Flertar resolve.

Por outro lado, Negociações normalmente envolvem todos os heróis interagindo com um ou mais NPCs importantes que podem oferecer informações, itens ou serviços capazes de mudar o rumo da aventura.  
Geralmente, isso envolve buscar um item de grande poder, um militante ou companheiro, os serviços de uma organização ou nação influente ou uma informação que cause uma reviravolta na trama. Convencer um Lich a emprestar o lendário _Codex Mortis_, persuadir um dragão a parar de atacar a torre de um mago ou convencer os generais de um exército inimigo a recuar significa que é hora de uma negociação.

Para negociar com sucesso, os heróis precisam apresentar argumentos persuasivos para convencer os NPCs. "Faça isso ou matamos você" é uma ameaça que pode acompanhar um Teste de Músculo com a Perícia Intimidar, mas não é uma tática de negociação.

### Limites da Negociação

Alguns jogadores podem achar que o sistema de Negociação deveria funcionar como uma espécie de controle mental. Eles não estão acostumados a ver NPCs como personagens complexos e podem tentar negociar em situações onde isso não faz sentido ou é literalmente impossível. Não importa quão eloquente um herói seja, nenhum argumento vai convencer o vil Lorde Syuul a abandonar o mal e virar jardineiro. Uma negociação tipicamente não pode convencer uma rainha a entregar sua coroa aos heróis e nomeá-los os novos governantes ou inspirar um dragão a entregar todo o seu tesouro. Negociações só funcionam quando os heróis pedem algo que o NPC está disposto a seriamente considerar dar a eles.

Negociação não é um processo que muda a personalidade de um NPC. Os heróis estão tentando fazer com que ele perceba que agir diferente ainda está dentro de seu caráter. Você pode ser capaz de fazer o até então leal tenente de um chefe maligno reconsiderar seus erros. É um clichê dramático clássico. Ainda assim, você não está mudando a personalidade dele - você está convencendo ele de que suas ações cruéis lhe cabem. "É isso quem você é? É assim que você quer ser lembrado?!"

Se alguns jogadores querem usar a Negociação como desculpa para que seus personagens digam "Faça o que mandamos, senão!", você pode lembrá-los de que não é assim que a maioria das pessoas, incluindo NPCs, funciona. Qualquer herói que comece com essa atitude provavelmente perderá a negociação antes mesmo que ela comece.

### A Ameaça de Violência

No mundo real, negociações raramente ocorrem com a ameaça de violência imediata. Embaixadores não costumam ir para as vias de fato. Mas este é um RPG de fantasia heroica, com heróis armados até os dentes e capazes de alterar a realidade com o poder da mente. A ameaça de violência já está implícita. Todos envolvidos sabem que os personagens podem sacar armas a qualquer momento.

O Diretor tipicamente assume que o potencial implícito para que a situação se torne violenta já está sendo considerado em qualquer Negociação. Entretanto, se os heróis quiserem tornar essa ameaça mais evidente, então eles saem do espaço da Negociação e entram em um tipo diferente de relacionamento - e provavelmente é hora de sacar armas.

Negociação é sobre persuadir alguém a ajudar você voluntariamente porque você convenceu ele de que alcançar seus objetivos é uma boa ideia. Colaborar com você é sábio ou óbvio ou pode fazê-lo parecer bem para outros. Um herói pode absolutamente ameaçar alguém com violência e forçá-lo a fazer o que quiser, mas estes é um estado incrivelmente temporário. Um NPC ameaçado não está fazendo o que foi pedido por vontade própria. Ele o está fazendo sobe ameaça de violência e irá agir de acordo apenas enquanto esta ameaça for evidente - depois disso, ele provavelmente voltará ao comportamento anterior assim que pensar que puder fazer isso.

## Atributos de Negociação

Durante a Negociação, o Diretor designa aos NPCs quatro atributos e recursos temporários - Interesse, Paciência, Motivações e Implicâncias. Os heróis pode conseguir um acordo favorável se maximizarem o Interesse de um NPC ao apresentarem argumentos que apelam a suas Motivações e evitam suas Implicâncias - mas precisam fazer tudo isso antes que a Paciência do NPC acabe.

### Interesse

O Interesse de um NPC representa o quão disposto ele está a fazer um acordo com os heróis. O Interesse é medido em uma escala de 0 (sem Interesse) a 5 (Interesse máximo). Quando uma Negociação começa, o Interesse de um NPC está entre 1 e 4. Se o Interesse do NPC chegar a 5, ele faz uma oferta final e a Negociação termina (veja Continuar ou Parar, abaixo). Se o Interesse cair para 0, ele encerra a Negociação sem oferecer nada aos heróis.

O Interesse aumenta ou diminui durante a Negociação, dependendo dos argumentos feitos pelos heróis.

### Paciência

A Paciência de um NPC representa quanto tempo e esforço ele está disposto a dedicar à Negociação. A Paciência é medida em uma escala de 0 a 5, com cada NPC começando a Negociação com Paciência maior que 0. Se a Paciência de um NPC chegar a 0, ele faz uma oferta final e a Negociação termina (veja Continuar ou Parar).

A Paciência pode diminuir a cada argumento feito pelos heróis durante a Negociação.

#### Idioma e Paciência

Se um ou mais heróis envolvidos na Negociação falarem o Idioma nativo do NPC (excluindo Caeliano), a Paciência do NPC aumenta em 1 no início da Negociação (até o máximo de 5). Se três ou mais heróis falam o Idioma nativo do NPC, a Paciência aumenta em 2 (até o máximo de 5). Capítulo 4: Antecedentes tem mais informações sobre alguns dos Idiomas do jogo.

### Motivações

Cada NPC possui pelo menos duas Motivações às quais os heróis podem apelar em seus argumentos. Argumentos que apelam a uma Motivação do NPC fazem um Lançamento de Poder mais fácil para aumentar o Interesse do NPC. Argumentos que não apelam a uma Motivação fazem um Lançamento de Poder mais difícil. Veja Fazendo Argumentos para mais informações.

Cada Motivação só pode ser utilizada com sucesso uma vez por Negociação. Para apelar com sucesso a uma Motivação, os heróis devem usá-la em um argumento sem mencionar uma Implicância do NPC ou serem pegos mentindo.

### Implicâncias

Implicâncias são Motivações que causam raiva, desconforto, vergonha, medo ou outras respostas negativas em um NPC. Usar uma Implicância em um argumento reduz o Interesse e a Paciência do NPC. Cada NPC tem pelo menos uma Implicância e muitos têm duas ou mais.

Implicâncias e Motivações são dois lados da mesma moeda. Elas são apresentadas abaixo como uma lista única, pois o que pode ser uma Motivação para um NPC pode ser uma Implicância para outro. Sempre que os heróis fazem um argumento, correm o risco de esbarrar em uma Implicância, a menos que tenham feito uma boa pesquisa ou saibam entender bem o NPC.

### Lista de Motivações e Implicâncias

Um NPC pode ter qualquer uma das doze Motivações ou Implicâncias a seguir.

#### Benevolência

Um NPC com Motivação de Benevolência acredita em compartilhar o que tem com os outros. No entanto, um NPC envolvido em uma Negociação precisa ter limites em sua Benevolência, para que não simplesmente dê aos heróis o que eles querem.

Às vezes a Benevolência de um NPC pode se estender apenas a um grupo específico de pessoas, como um capitão pirata benevolente que divide seu saque livremente com a tripulação - mas ainda assim está saqueando! Outras vezes, a caridade de um NPC pode ser limitada pelo fato de que ele não tem muito a oferecer. Um NPC benevolente pode hesitar em ajudar os heróis porque acredita que seus recursos limitados fariam mais diferença em outro lugar.

Um NPC com a Implicância de Benevolência tem uma visão cínica do mundo, acreditando que nenhuma criatura tem direito a nada apenas por estar viva. A ideia de ajudar os outros por ser a coisa certa a se fazer é absurda, imatura ou ingênua, algo a ser ridicularizado ou suprimido.

Argumentos que apelam à Motivação de Benevolência defendem que, se o NPC fizer um acordo com os heróis, as pessoas de quem o NPC gosta sairão beneficiadas. Exemplos de argumentos incluem:

- “Se você nos emprestar a Espada de Agathor, podemos tornar Capital mais segura para sua guilda ao usá-la para derrotar seus inimigos.”
- “Se você nos teletransportar para a caverna do dragão, daremos metade do tesouro do monstro depois que cortarmos sua cabeça. Isso pode beneficiar gerações de alunos da sua academia!”

#### Descoberta

Um NPC com Motivação de Descoberta deseja aprender novos conhecimentos, explorar locais esquecidos, fazer descobertas por meio de experimentos ou encontrar artefatos perdidos ao tempo. Sua curiosidade e busca por conhecimento podem estar ligadas a um objetivo específico, como buscar a cura para uma doença rara ou encontrar um portal para um mundo distante. Ou pode ser que ele seja simplesmente uma pessoa naturalmente curiosa que quer entender tudo o que puder sobre a Timescape.
